THE STORY of an AFRICAN FARM 
 A novel . 


 BY 
 RALPH IRON .

 " we must see the first image which the external world cast upon the dark mirror of his mind ; or must hear the first word which awaken the sleep power of thought , and stand by his early effort , if we would understand the prejudice , the habit , and the passion that will rule his life . the entire man be , so to speak , to be find in the cradle of the child . " 

 ALEXIS DE TOCQUEVILLE . 



 the story of an AFRICAN FARM 

 PART I. 

 CHAPTER I. SHADOWS from child - LIFE . 

 the Watch . 

 the 
 full african moon pour down its light from the blue sky into the wide , lonely plain . the dry , sandy earth , with its coating of stunted " karroo " bush a few inch high , the low hill that skirt the plain , the milk - bush with their long finger - like leaf , all be touch by a weird and an almost oppressive beauty as they lie in the white light . 


 in one spot only be the solemn monotony of the plain break . near the centre a small 

 solitary " kopje " rise . alone it lie there , a heap of round ironstone pile one upon another , as over some giant 's grave . here and there a few tuft of grass or small succulent plant have spring up among its stone , and on the very summit a clump of prickly - pear lift their thorny arm , and reflect , as from mirror , the moonlight on their broad fleshy leaf . at the foot of the " kopje " lie the homestead . first , the stone - wall " sheep kraal " and Kaffir hut ; beyond they the dwelling - house a square , red - brick building with thatched roof . even on its bare red wall , and the wooden ladder that lead up to the loft , the moonlight cast a kind of dreamy beauty , and quite etherealize the low brick wall that run before the house , and which enclose a bare patch of sand and two straggle sun - flower . on the zinc roof of the great open waggon - house , on the roof of the outbuilding that jut from its side , the moonlight glint with a quite peculiar brightness , till it seem 

 that every rib in the metal be of burnish silver . 

 Sleep rule everywhere , and the homestead be not less quiet than the solitary plain . 
 in the farm - house , on her great wooden bedstead , Tant ' Sannie , the boer - woman , roll heavily in her sleep . 
 she have go to bed , as she always do , in her clothe , and the night be warm and the room close , and she dream bad dream . not of the ghost and devil that so haunt her wake thought ; not of her second husband , the consumptive Englishman , whose grave lie away beyond the ostrich - camp , nor of her first , the young boer ; but only of the sheep 's trotter she have eat for supper that night . she dream that one stick fast in her throat , and she roll her huge form from side to side , and snort horribly . 

 in the next room , where the maid have forget to close the shutter , the white moonlight fall in in a flood , and make it light as day . 

 there be two small bed against the wall . in one lie a yellow - haired child , with a low forehead and a face of freckle ; but the love moonlight hide defect here as elsewhere , and show only the innocent face of a child in its first sweet sleep . 

 the figure in the companion bed belong of right to the moonlight , for it be of quite elfin - like beauty . the child have drop her cover on the floor , and the moonlight look in at the naked little limb . presently she open her eye and look at the moonlight that be bath she . 
 " Em ! " she call to the sleeper in the other bed ; but receive no answer . then she draw the cover from the floor , turn her pillow , and pull the sheet over her head , go to sleep again . 

 only in one of the outbuilding that jut from the waggon - house there be some one who be not asleep . the room be dark ; door and 

 shutter be close ; not a ray of light enter anywhere . the german overseer , to whom the room belong , lie sleep soundly on his bed in the corner , his great arm fold , and his bushy grey and black beard rise and fall on his breast . but one in the room be not asleep . two large eye look about in the darkness , and two small hand be smooth the patchwork quilt . the boy , who sleep on a box under the window , have just awaken from his first sleep . he draw the quilt up to his chin , so that little peer above it but a great head of silky black curl and the two black eye . he star about in the darkness . nothing be visible , not even the outline of one worm - eat rafter , nor of the deal table , on which lie the Bible from which his father have read before they go to bed . no one could tell where the tool - box be , and where the fire - place . there be something very impressive to the child in the complete darkness . 


 at the head of his father 's bed hang a great 

 silver hunting watch . it tick loudly . the boy listen to it , and begin mechanically to count . tick tick tick ! one , two , three , four ! he lose count presently , and only listen . tick tick tick tick ! 


 it never wait ; it go on inexorably ; and every time it tick 
 a man die 
 ! he raise himself a little on his elbow and listen . he wish it would leave off . 

 how many time have it tick since he come to lie down ? a thousand time , a million time , perhaps . 
 he try to count again , and sit up to listen well . 
 " die , die , die ! " say the watch ; " die , die , die ! " 
 he hear it distinctly . where be they go to , all those people ? 
 he lie down quickly , and pull the cover up over his head : but presently the silky curl reappear . 

 " die , die , die ! " say the watch ; " die , die , die ! " 

 he think of the word his father have read that evening " 
 for wide be the gate , and broad be the way , that leadeth to destruction and many there be which go in thereat . 
 " 

 " many , many , many ! " say the watch . 

 " 
 because strait be the gate , and narrow be the way , that leadeth unto life , and few there be that find it . 
 " 

 " few , few , few ! " say the watch . 

 the boy lie with his eye wide open . he see before he a long stream of people , a great dark multitude , that move in one direction ; then they come to the dark edge of the world and go over . he see they pass on before he , and there be nothing that could stop they . he think of how that stream have roll on through all the long age of the past how the old Greeks and Romans have go over ; the countless million of China and India , they be 

 go over now . since he have come to bed , how many have go ! 

 and the watch say , " eternity , eternity , eternity ! " 
 " stop they ! stop they ! " cry the child . 
 and all the while the watch keep tick on ; just like God 's will , that never change or alter , you may do what you please . 
 great bead of perspiration stand on the boy 's forehead . he climb out of bed and lie with his face turn to the mud floor . 
 " oh , God , God ! save they ! " he cry in agony . " only some , only a few ! only for each moment I be pray here one ! " he fold his little hand upon his head . " God ! God ! save they ! " 
 he grovel on the floor . 

 oh , the long , long age of the past , in which they have go over ! oh , the long , long future , in which they would pass away ! oh , 

 God ! the long , long , long eternity , which have no end ! 

 the child weep ; and creep close to the ground . 


 the Sacrifice . 

 the 
 farm by daylight be not as the farm by moonlight . the plain be a weary flat of loose red sand , sparsely cover by dry karroo - bush , that crack beneath the tread like tinder , and show the red earth everywhere . here and there a milk - bush lift its pale - colour rod , and in every direction the ant and beetle run about in the blaze sand . the red wall of the farm - house , the zinc roof of the out - building , the stone wall of the " kraal , " all reflect the fierce sunlight , till the eye ache and blench . no tree or shrub be to be see far or near . the two sunflower that stand 

 before the door , out - star by the sun , droop their brazen face to the sand ; and the little cicada - like insect cry aloud among the stone of the " kopje . " 

 the boer - woman , see by daylight , be even less lovely than , when , in bed , she roll and dream . she sit on a chair in the great front room , with her foot on a wooden stove , and wipe her flat face with the corner of her apron , and drink coffee , and in Cape Dutch swear that the beloved weather be damned . less lovely , too , by daylight be the dead Englishman 's child , her little step - daughter , upon whose freckle and low , wrinkle forehead the sunlight have no mercy . 
 " Lyndall , " the child say to her little orphan cousin , who sit with she on the floor thread bead , " how be it your bead never fall off your needle ? " 
 " I try , " say the little one gravely , moisten her tiny finger . " that be why . " 

 the overseer , see by daylight , be a huge german , wear a shabby suit , and with a childish habit of rub his hand and nod his head prodigiously when pleased at anything . he stand out at the kraal in the blaze sun , explain to two Kaffer boy the approach end of the world . the boy , as they cut the cake of dung , wink at each other , and work as slowly as they possibly could ; but the German never see it . 

 away , beyond the " kopje , " Waldo his son herd the ewe and lamb a small and dusty herd powder all over from head to foot with red sand , wear a ragged coat and shoe of undressed leather , through whose hole the toe look out . his hat be too large , and have sink down to his eye , conceal completely the silky black curl . it be a curious small figure . his flock give he little trouble . it be too hot for they to move far ; they gather round every little milk - bush , as though they 

 hop to find shade , and stand there motionless in clump . he himself creep under a shelving rock that lie at the foot of the " kopje , " stretch himself on his stomach , and wave his dilapidated little shoe in the air . 


 soon , from the blue bag where he keep his dinner , he produce a fragment of slate , an arithmetic , and a pencil . proceed to put down a sum with solemn and earnest demeanour , he begin to add it up aloud : " six and two be eight and four be twelve and two be fourteen and four be eighteen . " here he pause . " and four be eighteen and four be eighteen . " the last be very much drawled . slowly the pencil slip from his finger , and the slate follow it into the sand . for a while he lie motionless , then begin mutter to himself , fold his little arm , lay his head down upon they , and might have be asleep , but for the muttering sound that from time to time proceed from he . a curious old ewe come to sniff at he ; but it be 

 long before he raise his head . when he do , he look at the far - off hill with his heavy eye . 


 " ye shall receive ye shall receive 
 shall , shall , shall , 
 " he mutter . 

 he sit up then . slowly the dulness and heaviness melt from his face ; it become radiant . Mid - day have come now , and the sun 's ray be pour down vertically ; the earth throb before the eye . 

 the boy stand up quickly , and clear a small space from the bush which cover it . look carefully , he find twelve small stone of somewhat the same size ; kneel down , he arrange they carefully on the clear space in a square pile , in shape like an altar . then he walk to the bag where his dinner be keep ; in it be a mutton chop and a large slice of brown bread . the boy take they out and turn the bread over in his hand , deeply consider it . finally he throw it away and walk to the altar with the meat , and lay it down on 

 the stone . close by in the red sand he kneel down . sure , never since the beginning of the world be there so ragged and so small a priest . he take off his great hat and place it solemnly on the ground , then close his eye and fold his hand . he pray aloud . 

 " oh , God , my Father , I have make Thee a sacrifice . I have only twopence , so I can not buy a lamb . if the lamb be mine , I would give Thee one ; but now I have only this meat ; it be my dinner - meat . please , my Father , send fire down from heaven to burn it . Thou hast say , Whosoever shall say unto this mountain , be thou cast into the sea , nothing doubt , it shall be do . I ask for the sake of Jesus Christ . amen . " 

 he kneel down with his face upon the ground , and he fold his hand upon his curl . the fierce sun pour down its heat upon his head and upon his altar . when he look up he know what he should see the glory of God ! for fear his very heart stand still , his breath 

 come heavily ; he be half suffocated . he dare not look up . then at last he raise himself . above he be the quiet blue sky , about he the red earth ; there be the clump of silent ewe and his altar that be all . 

 he look up nothing break the intense stillness of the blue overhead . he look round in astonishment , then he bow again , and this time long than before . 
 when he raise himself the second time all be unaltered . only the sun have melt the fat of the little mutton chop , and it run down upon the stone . 
 then , the third time he bow himself . when at last he look up , some ant have come to the meat on the altar . he stand up and drive they away . then he put his hat on his hot curl , and sit in the shade . he clasp his hand about his knee . he sit to watch what would come to pass . the glory of the Lord God Almighty ! he know he should see it . 


 " my dear God be try I , " he say ; and he sit there through the fierce heat of the afternoon . still he watch and wait when the sun begin to slope , and when it near the horizon and the sheep begin to cast long shadow across the 

 karro 
 karroo 

 , he still sit there . he hop when the first ray touch the hill till the sun dip behind they and be go . then he call his ewe together , and break down the altar , and throw the meat far , far away into the field . 

 he walk home behind his flock . his heart be heavy . he reason so : " God can not lie . I have faith . no fire come . I be like Cain I be not his . he will not hear my prayer . God hat I . " 
 the boy 's heart be heavy . when he reach the " kraal " gate the two girl meet he . 

 " come , " say the yellow - haired em , " let we play " coop.í there be still time before it get quite dark . you , Waldo , go and hide on the 

 " kopjeí ; Lyndall and I will shut eye here , and we will not look . " 

 the girl hide their face in the stone wall of the sheep - kraal , and the boy clamber half way up the " kopje . " he crouch down between two stone and give the call . just then the milk - herd come walk out of the cow - kraal with two pail . he be an ill - look Kaffir . 
 " ah ! " think the boy , " perhaps he will die to - night , and go to hell ! I must pray for he , I must pray ! " 

 then he think " where be 
 I 
 go to ? " and he pray desperately . 


 " ah ! this be not right at all , " little Em say , peep between the stone , and find he in a very curious posture . " what 
 be 
 you do Waldo ? it be not the play , you know . you should run out when we come to the white stone . ah , you do not play nicely . " 


 " I I will play nicely now , " say the boy , 

 come out and stand sheepishly before they ; " I I only forgot ; I will play now . " 

 " he have be to sleep , " say freckle Em . 
 " no , " say beautiful little Lyndall , look curiously at he ; " he have be cry . " 
 she never make a mistake . 


 the Confession . 

 one 
 night , two year after , the boy sit alone on the " kopje . " he have creep softly from his father 's room and come there . he often do , because , when he pray or cry aloud , his father might awake and hear he ; and none know his great sorrow , and none know his grief , but he himself , and he bury they deep in his heart . 


 he turn up the brim of his great hat and look at the moon , but most at the leaf of the prickly pear that grow just before he . they glint , and glint , and glint , just 

 like his own heart cold , so hard , and very wicked . his physical heart have pain also ; it seem full of little bit of glass , that hurt . he have sit there for half an hour , and he dare not go back to the close house . 

 he feel horribly lonely . there be not one thing so wicked as he in all the world , and he know it . he fold his arm and begin to cry not aloud ; he sob without make any sound , and his tear leave scorch mark where they fall . he could not pray ; he have pray night and day for so many month ; and to - night he could not pray . when he leave off cry , he hold his ache head with his brown hand . if one might have go up to he and touch he kindly , poor , ugly little thing ! I think his heart be well nigh break . 

 with his swollen eye he sit there on a flat stone at the very top of the " kopje " ; and the tree , with every one of its wicked leaf , blink , and blink , and blink at he . 

 presently he begin to cry again , and then stop his crying to look at it . he be quiet for a long while , then he kneel up slowly and bend forward . there be a secret he have carry in his heart for a year . he have not dare to look at it ; he have not whisper it to himself , but for a year he have carry it . " I hate God ! " he say . the wind take the word and run away with they , among the stone , and through the leaf of the prickly pear . he think it die away half down the " kopje . " he have tell it now ! 

 " I love Jesus Christ , but I hate God . " 
 the wind carry away that sound as it have do the first . then he get up and button his old coat about he . he know he be certainly lose now ; he do not care . if half the world be to be lose , why not he too ? he would not pray for mercy any more . well so well to know certainly . it be end now . well so . 

 he begin scramble down the side of the " kopje " to go home . 
 well so ! but oh , the loneliness , the agonize pain ! for that night , and for night on night to come ! the anguish that sleep all day on the heart like a heavy worm , and wake up at night to feed ! 
 there be some of we who in after year say to Fate , " now deal we your hard blow , give we what you will ; but let we never again suffer as we suffer when we be child . " 
 the barb in the arrow of childhood 's suffering be this its intense loneliness , its intense agony . 




 CHAPTER II . 
 plan and BUSHMAN - PAINTINGS . 

 AT 
 last come the year of the great drought , the year of eighteen - sixty - two , I think . from end to end of the land the earth cry for water . man and beast turn their eye to the pitiless sky , that like the roof of some brazen oven arch overhead . on the farm , day after day , month after month , the water in the dam fall lower and low ; the sheep die in the field ; the cattle , scarcely able to crawl , totter as they move from spot to spot in search of food . week after week , month after month , the sun look down from the cloudless sky , till the karroo - bush be leafless stick , break into the earth , and the earth itself be naked and bare ; 

 and only the milk - bush , like old hag , point their shrivelled finger heavenward , pray for the rain that never come . 


 it be on an afternoon of a long day in that thirsty summer , that on the side of the " kopje " furth from the homestead the two girl sit . they be somewhat grow since the day when they play hide - and - seek there , but they be mere child still . 
 their dress be of dark coarse stuff ; their common blue pinafore reach to their ankle , and on their foot they wear home - make " vel - schoen . " 
 they sit under a shelve rock , on the surface of which be still visible some old Bushman painting , their red and black pigment have be preserve through long year from wind and rain by the overhang ledge ; grotesque oxen , elephant , rhinoceros , and a one - horn beast , such as no man ever have see or ever shall . 

 the girl sit with their back to the painting . in their lap be a few fern and ice - plant leaf , which by dint of much search they have gather under the rock . 
 em take off her big brown kappje and begin vigorously to fan her red face with it ; but her companion bent low over the leaf in her lap , and at last take up an ice - plant leaf and fasten it on to the front of her blue pinafore with a pin . 
 " diamond must look as these drop do , " she say , carefully bend over the leaf , and crush one crystal drop with her delicate little finger . " when I , " she say , " be grow up , I shall wear real diamond , exactly like these in my hair . " 
 her companion open her eye and wrinkle her low forehead . 
 " where will you find they , Lyndall ? the stone be only crystal that we pick up yesterday . Old Otto say so . " 


 " and you think that I be go to stay 
 here 
 always ? " 

 the lip tremble scornfully . 
 " ah , no , " say her companion . " I suppose some day we shall go somewhere ; but now we be only twelve , and we can not marry till we be seventeen . four year , five that be a long time to wait . and we might not have diamond if we do marry . " 
 " and you think that I be go to stay here till then ? " 

 " well , where 
 be 
 you go ? " ask her companion . 

 the girl crush an ice - plant leaf between her finger . 

 " Tant ' Sannie be a miserable old woman , " she say . " your father marry she when he be die , because he think she would take well care of the farm , and of we , than an Englishwoman . he say we should be teach and send to school . now she save every 

 farthing for herself , buy we not even one old book . she do not ill - use we why ? because she be afraid of your father 's ghost . only this morning she tell she Hottentot that she would have beat you for break the plate , but that three night ago she hear a rustling and a grunting behind the pantry door , and know it be your father come to " spookí she . she be a miserable old woman , " say the girl , throw the leaf from she ; " but I intend to go to school . " 

 " and if she will not   let you ? " 
 " I shall make she . " 
 " how ? " 
 the child take not the slight notice of the last question , and fold her small arm across her knee . 
 " why do you want to go , Lyndall ? " 
 " there be nothing help in this world , " say the child slowly , " but to be very wise , and to know everything to be clever . " 

 " but I should not like to go to school ! " persist the small freckle face . 
 " and you do not need to . when you be seventeen this boer - woman will go ; you will have this farm and everything that be upon it for your own ; but I , " say Lyndall , " will have nothing . I must learn . " 

 " oh , Lyndall ! 
 I 
 will give you some of my sheep , " say em , with a sudden burst of pity generosity . 

 " I do not want your sheep , " say the girl slowly ; " I want thing of my own . when I be grow up , " she add , the flush on her delicate feature deepen at every word , " there will be nothing that I do not know . I shall be rich , very rich ; and I shall wear , not only for good , but every day , a pure white silk , and little rose - bud , like the lady in Tant ' Sannie 's bedroom , and my petticoat will be embroider , not only at the bottom , but all through . " 

 the lady in Tant ' Sannie 's bedroom be a gorgeous creature from a fashion - sheet , which the boer - woman , somewhere obtain , have paste up at the foot of her bed , to be profoundly admire by the child . 
 " it would be very nice , " say Em ; but it seem a dream of quite too transcendent a glory ever to be realize . 
 at this instant there appear at the foot of the " kopje " two figure the one , a dog , white and sleek , one yellow ear hang down over his left eye ; the other , his master , a lad of fourteen , and no other than the boy Waldo , grow into a heavy , slouch youth of fourteen . the dog mount the " kopje " quickly , his master follow slowly . he wear an aged jacket much too large for he , and roll up at the wrist , and , as of old , a pair of dilapidated " vel - schoen " and a feel hat . he stand before the two girl at last . 

 " what have you be do to - day ? " ask 

 Lyndall , lift her eye to his face . 

 " look after ewe and lamb below the dam . here ! " he say , hold out his hand awkwardly , " I bring they for you . " 
 there be a few green blade of tender grass . 
 " where do you find they ? " 
 " on the dam wall . " 
 she fasten they beside the leaf on her blue pinafore . 
 " they look nice there , " say the boy , awkwardly rub his great hand and watch she . 
 " yes ; but the pinafore spoil it all ; it be not pretty . " 
 he look at it closely . 
 " yes , the square be ugly ; but it look nice upon you beautiful . " 
 he now stand silent before they , his great hand hang loosely at either side . 

 " some one have come to - day , " he mumble out suddenly , when the idea strike he . 
 " who ? " ask both girl . 
 " an Englishman on foot . " 
 " what do he look like ? " ask Em .

 " do not   he tell you his name ? " 
 " yes Bonaparte Blenkins . " 

 " Bonaparte ! " say em , " why that be like the reel Hottentot Hans play on the violin 


 " Bonaparte , Bonaparte , my wife be sick ;

 it be a funny name . " 

 " there be a live man call Bonaparte once , " say she of the great eye . 
 " ah yes , I know , " say Em " the poor prophet whom the lion eat . I be always so sorry for he . " 

 her companion cast a quiet glance upon she . 
 " he be the great man who ever live , " she say " the man I like well . " 
 " and what do he do ? " ask Em , conscious that she have make a mistake , and that her prophet be not the man . 
 " he be one man , only one , " say her little companion slowly , " yet all the people in the world fear he . he be not bear great , he be common as we be ; yet he be master of the world at last . once he be only a little child , then he be a lieutenant , then he be a general , then he be an emperor . when he say a thing to himself he never forget it . he wait , and wait , and wait , and it come at last . " 
 " he must have be very happy , " say em .

 one 
 . they send he to an island on the sea , a lonely island , and keep he there fast . he be one man , and they be many , and they be terrify at he . it be glorious ! " say the child . 

 " and what then ? " say Em . 
 " then he be alone there in that island with man to watch he always , " say her companion , slowly and quietly , " and in the long lonely night he use to lie awake and think of the thing he have do in the old day , and the thing he would do if they let he go again . in the day when he walk near the shore it seem to he that the sea all around he be a cold chain about his body press he to death . " 
 " and then ? " say Em , much interested . 

 " he die there in that island ; he never get away . " 
 " it be rather a nice story , " say Em ; " but the end be sad . " 
 " it be a terrible , hateful ending , " say the little teller of the story , lean forward on her fold arm ; " and the bad be , it be true . I have notice , " add the child very deliberately , " that it be only the make - up story that end nicely ; the true one all end so . " 
 as she speak the boy 's dark , heavy eye rest on her face . 
 " you have read it , have you not ? " 
 he nod . " yes ; but the brown history tell only what he do , not what he think . "

 what he think . book do not tell everything . " 

 " no , " say the boy , slowly draw nearer to she and sit down at her foot . " what you want to know they never tell . " 

 then the child fall into silence , till Doss , the dog , grow uneasy at its long continuance , sniff at one and the other , and his master break forth suddenly , 

 " if

" he say , move his hand out over the surround object " then we would know something . this " kopje , í if it could tell we how it come here ! the " Physical Geographyí say , " he go on most rapidly and confusedly , " that what be dry land now be once lake ; and what I think be this these low hill be once the shore of a lake ; this " kopje " be some of the stone that be at the bottom , roll together by the water . but there be this how do the water come to make one heap here alone , in the centre of the plain ?  now I know the water must have do it ; but how ? it be very wonderful . do one little stone come first , and stop the other as they roll ? " say the boy with earnestness , in a low voice , more as speak to himself than to they .

 " by want . " 
 " but how do the wanting bring it here ? " 
 " because it do . " 
 the last word be utter with the air of one who produce a clinching argument . what effect it have on the questioner be not evident , for he make no reply , and turn away from she . 
 draw close to Lyndall 's foot , he say after a while , in a low voice ,

 talk with you ? sometimes , " he add in a yet low tone , " I lie under there

" 


 the child have turn round and look at the picture . 
 " he use to kneel here naked , painting , painting , painting ; and he wonder at the thing he make himself , " say the boy , rise and move his hand in deep excitement . " now the Boers have shoot they all , so that we never see a little yellow face peep out among the stone ; and the wild buck have go , and those day , and we be here . but we will be go soon , and only the stone will be on here , look at everything like they look now . of course I know , " the fellow add slowly , " that it be I who be think , not they who be talk ; but it seem as though it be they . have it never seem to you that thing that do not live be talkig to you , Lyndall ? "

 " my friend , " say Bonaparte , " it would give I the profound felicity , the most unbounded satisfaction ; but in these wear - out habiliment , in these deteriorated garment , it would not be possible , it would not be fitting that I should officiate in service of one whom , for respect , we shall not name . no , my friend , I will remain here ; and , while you be assemble yourselves together in the presence of the Lord , I , in my solitude , will think of and pray for you . no ; I will remain here ! " 

 it be a touching picture the solitary man there pray for they . the german clear his hand from the meal , and go to the chest from which he have take the black hat . after a little careful feeling about , he produce a black cloth coat , trowser , and waistcoat , which he lay on the table , smile knowingly . they

 " I have only wear they once . they might serve ; they might be endure . "

 CHAPTER V. 
 SUNDAY SERVICES . 

 SERVICE NO . I. 

 THE 
 boy Waldo kiss the page of his book and look up . far over the flat lie the " kopje , " a mere speck ; the sheep wander quietly from bush to bush ; the stillness of the early Sunday rest everywhere , and the air be fresh .

 SERVICE NO . II . 

 in 
 the front room of the farmhouse sit Tant ' Sannie in her elbow - chair . in her hand be her great brass - clasp hymn - book , round her neck be a clean white handkerchief , under her foot be a wooden stove . there too sit Em and Lyndall , in clean pinafore and new shoe . there too be the spruce Hottentot in a starch white " cappje , " and her husband on the other side of the door , with his wool oil and very much comb out , and star at his new leather boot . the Kaffir servant be not there because Tant ' Sannie hold they be descend from ape , and need no salvation . but the rest be gather for the Sunday service , and wait the officiator . 


 meanwhile Bonaparte and the german approach arm in arm Bonaparte resplendent in the black cloth clothe , a spotless shirt , and a spotless collar ; the german in the old salt - and - pepper , cast shy glance of admiration at his companion . 
 at the front door Bonaparte remove his hat with much dignity , raise his shirt collar , and enter . to the centre table he walk , put his hat solemnly down by the big Bible , and bow his head over it in silent prayer . 
 the boer - woman look at the Hottentot , and the Hottentot look at the boer - woman . 

 there be one thing on earth for which Tant ' Sannie have a profound reverence , which exercise a subduing influence over she , which make she for the time a well woman that thing be new , shin black cloth . it make she think of the " predikant ; " it make her think of the elder who sit in the top pew of the church on Sundays , with the hair so nicely oil , so holy 

 and respectable , with their little swallow - tail coat ; it make she think of heaven , where everything be so holy and respectable , and nobody wear tan - cord , and the little angel have a black tail - coat . she wish she have not   call he a thief and a roman Catholic . she hop the German have not   tell he . she wonder where those clothe be when he come in rag to her door . there be no doubt , he be a very respectable man , a gentleman . 

 the German begin to read a hymn . at the end of each line Bonaparte groan , and twice at the end of every verse . 

 the boer - woman have often hear of person groan during prayer , to add a certain poignancy and finish to they ; she would have look upon it as no especial sign of grace in any one ; but to groan at hymn - time ! she be startle . she wonder if he remember that she shake her fist in his face . this be a man of God . they kneel down to pray . the boer - woman 

 weigh two hundred and fifty pound , and could not kneel . she sit in her chair , and peep between her cross finger at the stranger 's back . she could not understand what he say ; but he be in earnest . he shake the chair by the back rail till it make quite a little dust on the mud floor . 

 when they rise from their knee Bonaparte solemnly seat himself in the chair and open the Bible . he blow his nose , pull up his shirt collar , smooth the leaf , stroke down his capacious waistcoat , blow his nose again , look solemnly round the room , then begin , 
 " all liar shall have their part in the lake which burneth with fire and brimstone , which be the second death . " 
 have read this portion of Scripture , Bonaparte pause impressively , and look all round the room . 

 " I shall not , my dear friend , " he say , " long detain you . much of our precious time have 

 already flee blissfully from we in the voice of thanksgiving and the tongue of praise . a few , a very few word be all I shall address to you , and may they be as a rod of iron divide the bone from the marrow , and the marrow from the bone . 

 " in the first place : what be a liar ? " 
 the question be put so pointedly , and follow by a pause so profound , that even the Hottentot man leave off look at his boot and open his eye , though he understand not a word . 
 " I repeat , " say Bonaparte , " what be a liar ? " 
 the sensation be intense ; the attention of the audience be rivet . 

 " have you any of you ever see a liar , my dear friend ? " there be a still long pause . " I hope not ; I truly hope not . but I will tell you what a liar be . I know a liar once a little boy who live in Cape Town , in Short Market 

 Street . his mother and I sit together one day , discourse about our soul . 

 " " here , Sampson , í say his mother , " go and buy sixpence of " meiboss " from the Malay round the corner.í 
 " when he come back she say : " how much have you got?í 
 " " Five , í he say . 
 " he be afraid if he say six and a half she would ask for some . and , my friend , that be a lie . the half of a " meibossí stuck in his throat and he die and be bury . and where do the soul of that little liar go to , my friend ? it go to the lake of fire and brimstone . this bring I to the second point of my discourse . 
 " what be a lake of fire and brimstone ? I will tell you , my friend , " say Bonaparte condescendingly . " the imagination unaide can not conceive it : but by the help of the Lord I will put it before your mind 's eye . 

 " I be travel in Italy once on a time ; 

 I come to a city call Rome , a vast city , and near it be a mountain which spit forth fire . its name be Etna . now , there be a man in that city of Rome who have not the fear of God before his eye , and he love a woman . the woman die , and he walk up that mountain spitting fire , and when he get to the top , he throw himself in at the hole that be there . the next day I go up . I be not afraid ; the Lord preserve his servant . and in their hand shall they bear thee up , lest at any time thou fall into a volcano . it be dark night when I get there , but in the fear of the Lord I walk to the edge of the yawning abyss , and look in . that sight that sight , my friend , be impress upon my most indelible memory . I look down into the lurid depth upon an incandescent lake , a melt fire , a seething sea ; the billow roll from side to side , and on their fiery crest toss the white skeleton of the suicide . the heat have burn the flesh from off 

 the bone ; they lie as a light cork upon the melt , fiery wave . one skeleton hand be raise upward , the finger pointing to heaven ; the other , with outstretched finger , point downward , as though it would say , " I go below , but you , Bonaparte , may soar above.í I gaze ; I stand entrance . at that instant there be a crack in the lurid lake ; it swell , expand , and the skeleton of the suicide disappear , to be see no more by mortal eye . " 

 here again Bonaparte rest , and then continue 

 " the lake of melted stone rise in the crater , it swell higher and high at the side , it stream forth at the top . I have presence of mind ; near I be a rock ; I stand upon it . the fiery torrent be vomit out and stream on either side of I . and through that long and terrible night I stand there alone upon that rock , the glowing , fiery lava on every hand a monument of the long - suffer and tender providence of 

 the Lord , who spar I that I might this day testify in your ear of he . 

 " now , my dear friend , let we deduce the lesson that be to be learn from this narrative . 
 " firstly : let we never commit suicide . the man be a fool , my friend , that man be insane , my friend , who would leave this earth , my friend . here be joy innumerable , such as it hath not enter into the heart of man to understand , my friend . here be clothe , my friend ; here be bed , my friend ; here be delicious food , my friend . our precious body be give we to love , to cherish . oh , let we do so ! oh , let we never hurt they ; but care for and love they , my friend ! " 
 every one be impressed , and Bonaparte proceed . 

 " thirdly ; let we not love too much . if that young man have not love that young woman , he would not have jump into Mount Etna . the good man of old never do so . be Jeremiah

 " " a charge to keep I have , 
 a God to glorify ; 
 a never - die soul to save , 
 and fit it for the sky . ' 


 " oh , beloved friend , remember the little boy and the " meibossí ; remember the young girl and the young man ; remember the lake , the fire , and the brimstone ; remember the suicide 's skeleton on the pitchy billow of Mount Etna ; remember the voice of warning that have this day sound in your ear ; and what I say to you I say to all watch ! may the Lord add his blessing ! "

 in the afternoon the German and Bonaparte sit before the door of the cabin . both smoke in complete silence Bonaparte with a book in his hand and his eye half close ; the german puff vigorously , and glance up now and again at the serene blue sky overhead .

 CHAPTER VIII . 
 he catch the OLD BIRD . 

 AT 
 four o'clock the next afternoon the german ride across the plain , return from his search for the lost sheep . he ride slowly , for he have be in the saddle since sunrise and be somewhat weary , and the heat of the afternoon make his horse sleepy as it pick its way slowly along the sandy road . every now and then a great red spider would start out of the karroo on one side of the path and run across to the other , but nothing else break the still monotony . presently , behind one of the high of the milk - bush that dot the roadside , the german catch sight of a Kaffir woman , seat there evidently for such shadow as the milk - bush 

 might afford from the slop ray of the sun . the German turn the horse 's head out of the road . it be not his way to pass a living creature without a word of greeting . come nearer , he find it be no other than the wife of the absconding Kaffir herd . she have a baby tie on her back by a dirty strip of red blanket ; another strip hardly large be twist round her waist , for the rest her black body be naked . she be a sullen , ill - look woman , with lip hideously protrude . 

 the German question she as to how she come there . she mutter in broken Dutch that she have be turn away . have she do evil ? she shake her head sullenly . have she have food give she ? she grunt a negative , and fan the fly from her baby . tell the woman to remain where she be , he turn his horse 's head to the road and ride off at a furious pace . 
 " hard - hearted ! cruel ! oh , my God ! be this the way ? be this charity ? "

 " you must try and get to the next farm , " say the German . 
 the woman shake her head ; she would sleep in the field .

" with that they will sleep warmly ; not so bad . ha , ha ! " say the German . and he ride home , nod his head in a manner that would have make any other man dizzy .

 have conclude this quaint production , he put it where the child would find it the next morning , and proceed to prepare his bundle . he never think of enter a protest against the loss of his good ; like a child , he submit , and weep . he have be there eleven year , and it be hard to go away . he spread open on the bed a blue handkerchief , and on it put one by one the thing he think most necessary and important a little bag of curious seed , which he mean to plant some day , an old german hymn - book , three misshapen stone that he greatly value , a Bible , a shirt and two handkerchief ; then there be room for nothing more . he tie up the bundle tightly and put it on a chair by his bed - side .

 but quiet as all place be , there be a quite peculiar quiet in the German 's room . though you strain your ear most carefully you catch no sound of breathing . 

 he be not go , for the old coat still hang on the chair the coat that be to be put on when he meet any one ; and the bundle and stick be ready for to - morrow 's long march . the old German himself lie there , his wavy black hair just touch with grey throw back upon the pillow . the old face be lie there alone in the dark , smile like a little child 's oh , so peacefully . there be a stranger whose come , they say , be bad than all the ill of life , from whose presence we flee away tremble ; but he come very tenderly sometimes . and it seem almost as though Death have know and love the old man , so gently it touch he . and how could it deal hardly 

 with he the love , simple , childlike old man ? 

 so it smooth out the wrinkle that be in the old forehead , and fix the pass smile , and seal the eye that they might not weep again ; and then the short sleep of time be melt into the long , long sleep of eternity . 
 " how have he grow so young in this one night ? " they say when they find he in the morning . 
 yes , dear old man ; to such as you time bring no age . you die with the purity and innocence of your childhood upon you , though you die in your grey hair .

 he see a ghost .

 but Bonaparte soon come to a conclusion as to the nature of the book and its content , by the application of a simple rule now largely act upon , but which , become universal , would save much thought and valuable time . it be of marvellous simplicity , of infinite utility , of universal applicability . it may easily be commit to memory and run thus : 

 whenever you come into contact with any book , person , or opinion of which you absolutely comprehend nothing , declare that book , person or opinion to be immoral . Bespatter it , vituperate against it , strongly insist that any man or woman harbour it be a fool or a knave , or both . carefully abstain from study it . do all that in you lie to annihilate that book , person , or opinion .

 the trouble of the young be soon over ; they leave no external mark . if you wound the tree in its youth the bark will quickly cover the gash ; but when the tree be very old , peel the bark off , look carefully , and you will see the scar there still . all that be bury be not dead .

 CHAPTER I. 
 Times and Seasons . 

 waldo 
 lie on his stomach on the sand . since he pray and howl to his God in the fuel - house three year have pass . 

 they say that in the world to come time be not measure out by month and year . neither be it here . the soul 's life have season of its own ; period not find in any calendar , time that year and month will not scan , but which be as deftly and sharply cut off from one another as the smoothly - arrange year which the earth 's motion yield we . 

 to stranger eye these division be not evident ; but each , look back at the little 

 track his consciousness illuminate , see it cut into distinct portion , whose boundary be the termination of mental state . 

 as man differ from man , so differ these soul ' year . the most material life be not devoid of they ; the story of the most spiritual be tell in they . and it may chance that some , look back , see the past cut out after this fashion : 

 I. 
 the year of infancy , where from the shadowy background of forgetfulness start out picture of startle clearness , disconnected , but brightly colour , and indelibly print in the mind . much that follow fade , but the colour of those baby - picture be permanent . 
 there rise , perhaps , a warm summer 's evening ; we be seat on the door - step ; we have yet the taste of the bread and milk in our mouth , and the red sunset be reflect in our basin . 

 then there be a dark night , where , wake with a nameless fear , we run from our own bed to another , creep close to some large figure , and be comfort . 
 then there be remembrance of the pride when , on some one 's shoulder , with our arm around their head , we ride to see the little pig . 
 remembrance of delight in the feel and smell of the first orange we ever see ; of sorrow which make we put up our lip , and cry hard , when one morning we run out to try and catch the dew - drop , and they melt and wet our little finger ; of almighty and despairing sorrow when we be lose behind the kraal , and can not see the house anywhere . 
 and then one picture start out more vividly than any . 

 there have be a thunder - storm ; the ground , as far as the eye can reach , be cover with white hail ; the cloud be go , and overhead a deep blue sky be show ; far off a great 

 rainbow rest on the white earth . we , stand in a window to look , feel the cool , unspeakably sweet wind blow in on we , and a feeling of longing come over we unutterable longing , we can not tell for what . we look at the white earth , and the rainbow , and the blue sky ; and oh , we want it , we want we do not know what . we cry as though our heart be break . when one lift our little body from the window we can not tell what ail we . we run away to play . 

 so look the first year . 


 II . 
 now the picture become continuous and connected . material thing still rule , but the spiritual and intellectual take their place . 

 in the dark night when we be afraid we pray and shut our eye . we press our finger very hard upon the lid , and see dark spot

 be 
 so . we be not satisfied ; we hate to learn ; we like well to build little stone house . we can build they as we please , and know the reason for they . 

 other joy too we have incomparably great . 
 we be run through with a shudder of delight when in the red sand we come on one of those white wax - flower that lie between their two green leaf flat on the sand . we hardly dare pick they , but we feel compel to do so ; and we smell and smell till the delight become almost pain . afterwards we pull the green leaf softly into piece to see the silk thread run across . 

 beyond the " kopje " grow some dull - green , 

 hairy - leave bush . we be so small they meet over our head ; and we sit among they , and talk to they , and kiss they , and they love we back . 


 one day we sit there and look up at the blue sky , and down at our fat little knee ; and suddenly it strike we , who be we ? this 
 I 
 , what be it ? we try to look in upon ourselves , and ourself beat back upon ourself . then we get up in great fear and run home as hard as we can . we can not   tell any one what frighten we . we never quite lose that feeling of 
 self 
 again . 



 III . 
 and then a new time rise . we be seven year old . we can read now read the Bible . good of all we like the story of Elijah in his cave at Horeb , and the still small voice . 

 one day , a notable one , we read on the 

 " kopje , " and discover the fifth chapter of Matthew , and read it all through . then we tuck the Bible under our arm and rush home . they do not   know it be wicked to take your thing again if some one take they , wicked to go to law , wicked to ! we be quite breathless when we get to the house ; we tell they we have discover a chapter they never hear of ; we tell they what it say . the old wise people tell we they know all about it . our discovery be a mare's - nest to they ; but to we it be very real . the ten commandment and the old " thou shalt " we have hear about long enough and do not   care about it ; but this new law set we on fire . we will deny ourself . our little waggon that we have make , we give to the little Kaffirs . we keep quiet when they throw sand at we   feeling , oh , so happy . we conscientiously put the crack tea - cup for ourselves at breakfast , and take the burn roaster - cake . we save our money , and buy threepence of tobacco 

 for the Hottentot maid who call we name . we be exotically virtuous . at night we be profoundly religious ; even the tick watch say , " eternity , eternity ! hell , hell , hell ! " and the silence talk of God . 

 occasionally , also , unpleasantly shrewd question begin to be ask by something , we know not what , in ourselves . we get to know he well afterward . we carry the question to the grow - up people . they give we answer ; we be more or less satisfied for the time . the grow - up people be very wise , and they say it be kind of God to make hell , and very loving of he to send man there ; and besides , he could not   help himself , and they be very wise , we think , so we believe they . 


 IV . 

 then a new time come of which the lead feature be , that the shrewd question be ask 

 louder . we carry they to the grow - up people ; they answer we , and we be 
 not 
 satisfied . 

 and now between we and the dear old world of the sens the spirit - world begin to peep in , and wholly cloud it over . what be the flower to we ? they be fuel wait for the great burning . we look at the wall of the farmhouse and the matter - of - fact sheep " kraal , " with the merry sunshine play over all , and do not see it . but we see a great white throne , and he that sit on it . around he stand a great multitude that no man can number , harper harp with their harp , a thousand time ten thousand , and thousand of thousand . how white be their robe , wash in the blood of the Lamb ! and the music rise higher , and rend the vault of heaven with its unutterable sweetness . and we , as we listen , ever and anon , as it sink on the sweetest , low note , hear a groan of the damned from below . we shudder in the sunlight . 

 " the torment , " say Jeremy Taylor , whose sermon our father read aloud in the evening , " comprise as many torment as the body of man have joint , sinew , artery ,   c. , be cause by that penetrate and real fire , of which this temporal fire be but a paint fire . what comparison will there be between burn for a hundred year ' space and to be burn without intermission as long as God be God ? " 

 we remember the sermon there in the sunlight . one come and ask why we sit there nod so moodily . ah , they do not see what we see . 


 " a moment 's time , a narrow space ,

 so say Wesley 's hymn , which we sing evening by evening . what matter sunshine and wall , man and book ? 


 " the thing which be see be temporal , but 

 the thing which be not see be eternal . " they be real . 

 the Bible we bear always in our breast ; its page be our food ; we learn to repeat it ; we weep much , for in sunshine and in shade , in the early morning or the late evening , in the field or in the house , the Devil walk with we . he come to a real person , copper - colour face , head a little on one side , forehead knit , ask question . believe I , it would be well to be follow by three deadly disease than by he . he be never silence , never satisfied without mercy . though the drop of blood stand out on your heart he will put his question . softly he come up   we be only a wee bit child , mark you ; " be it good of God to make hell ? be it kind of he to let no one be forgive unless Jesus Christ die ? "

 " do you love he ? " wait a little . " do 

 you love he ? you will be lose if you do not . " 

 we say we try to . 
 " but do you ? " then he go off . 
 it be nothing to he if we go quite mad with fear at our own wickedness . he ask on , the question Devil ; he care nothing what he say . we long to tell some one , that they may share our pain . we do not yet know that the cup of affliction be make with such a narrow mouth that only one lip can drink at a time , and that each man 's cup be make to match his lip . 

 one day we try to tell some one . then a grave head be shake solemnly at we . we be wicked , very wicked , they say we ought not to have such thought . God be good , very good . we be wicked , very wicked . that be the comfort we get . wicked ! oh , Lord ! do we not know it ? be it not the sense of our own exceeding wickedness that be dry up our 

 young heart , fill it with sand , make all life a dust - bin for we ? 

 wicked ? we know it ! too vile to live , too vile to die , too vile to creep over this , God 's earth , and move among his believe man . Hell be the one place for he who hat his master , and there we do not want to go . 
 and once again we try to seek for comfort . this time great eye look at we wonder , and lovely little lip say , 

 " if it make you so unhappy to think of these thing , why do you not think of 
 something else , and forget ? 
 " 

 forget ? we turn away and shrink into ourself . forget ? and think of other thing ? oh , God ! do they not understand that the material world be but a film , through every pore of which God 's awful spirit world be shin through on we , poor miserable little wretch that we be ? we keep as far from other as we can . 

 one night , we kneel in the window ; every one 

 else sleep , but we kneel reading by the moonlight . it be only a chapter of the prophet , tell how the choose people of God shall be carry on the Gentiles ' shoulder . surely the Devil might leave we alone ; there be not much to handle for he there . but presently we hear he . 

 " be it right there should be a choose people ? if you should be choose out , would it be right , fair ? " 
 how can we answer he ? we be feel so good till he come . we put our head down on the Bible and blister it with tear . then we fold our hand over our head and pray , till our tooth grind together . oh , that from that spirit - world , so real and yet so silent , that surround we , one word would come to guide we ! we be leave alone with this devil ; the angel do not come . suddenly we seize the Bible , turn it round and round , and say hurriedly , 
 " it will be God 's voice speak to we ; his voice as though we hear it . " 

 we yearn , oh , so hugrily , for a token from the inexorably silent one . 
 we turn the book , put our finger down on a page , and bend to read by the moonlight . it be God 's answer . we tremble . 
 " then fourteen year after I go up again to Jerusalem with Barnabas , and take Titus with I also . " 

 for an instant our imagination seize it ; we be twist , twirl , try to make an allegory . the fourteen year be fourteen month ; we be Paul and the devil be Barnabas , Titus be then a sudden loathing come to we : we be liar and hypocrite , we be try to deceive ourselves . what be Paul to we and Jerusalem ? who be Barnabas and Titus ? we know not the man . this be no answer . before we know we seize the book , swing it round our head , and fle it with all our might to the farth end of the room . we put down our head again and weep . youth and ignorance yearn for light : 

 be there anything else that can weep so ? it be as though the tear be drop of blood congeal beneath the eyelid ; nothing else be like those tear . after a long time , when we be weak with crying , and lie silent , by chance we knock against the wood that stop the break pane . it fall . upon our hot stiff face a sweet breath of wind blow . we raise our head , and with our swollen eye look out at the beautiful still world , and the sweet night wind blow in upon we , holy and gentle , like a love breath from the lip of God . over we a deep peace come , a calm , still joy ; the tear now flow readily and softly . oh , the unutterable gladness ! at last , at last we have find it ! " 
 the peace with God . 
 " " 
 the sense of sin forgive .

 the peace with God . 
 " " 
 the sense of sin forgive . 
 " Methodists and Revivalists say the word , and the mocking world shoot out its lip , and walk by smile " Hypocrite ! " 

 there be more fool and few hypocrite than the wise world dream of . hypocrite be rare as iceberg in the tropic ; fool common as buttercup beside a water - furrow : whether you go this way or that you tread on they ; you dare not look at your own reflection in the water but you see one . there be no can not phrase , rotten with age , but it be the dress of a live body ; none but at heart it signify a real bodily or mental condition . 

 after hour and night of frenzied fear of the supernatural , desire to appease the power above , a fierce quivering excitement in every inch of nerve and blood - vessel , there come a time when nature can not
