 long , and the spring long bent recoil . we sink down emasculate . up creep the deadly delicious calm . 


 " I have blot out as a cloud thy sin , and as a thick cloud thy trespass , and will remember they no more for ever . " we weep with soft transporting joy . 
 a few experience this ; many imagine they experience it , one here and there lie about it . in the main , " the peace with God ; a sense of sin forgive , " stand for a certain mental and physical reaction . its reality those know who have feel it . 
 and we , on that moonlight night , put down our head on the window , " oh , God ! we be happy , happy ; thy child forever . oh , thank you , God ! " and we drop asleep . 
 next morning the Bible we kiss . we be God 's forever . we go out to work , and it go happily all day , happily all night ; but hardly so happily , not happily at all , the next day ; and the next night the devil ask we , " where be your Holy Spirit ? " 
 we can not tell . 

 so month by month , summer and winter , the old life go on reading , pray , weeping , pray . they tell we we become utterly stupid . we know it . even the multiplication table we learn with so much care we forget . the physical world recede far and far from we . truly we love not the world , neither the thing that be in it . across the bound of sleep our grief follow we . when we wake in the night we be sit up in bed weep bitterly , or find ourself outside in the moonlight , dress , and walk up and down , and wring our hand , and we can not tell how we come there . so pass two year , as man reckon they . 


 V. 
 then a new time . 
 before we there be three course possible to go mad , to die , to sleep . 

 we take the latter course ; nature take it for we . 
 all thing take rest in sleep ; the beast , bird , the very flower close their eye , and the stream be freeze in winter . all thing take rest in sleep ; then why not the human reason also ? so we drop asleep , and in that sleep a beautiful dream rise for we . though you hear all the dream of man , you will hardly find a pretty one than ours . it run so : 
 in the centre of all thing be a Mighty Heart , which , have beget all thing , love they ; and , have bear they into life , beat with great throb of love towards they . no death for his dear insect , no hell for his loved man , no burn up for his dear world his own , own world ! in the end all will be well . do not ask we how we make our dream tally with fact ; the glory of a dream be this that it despise fact , and make its own . our dream save we from go mad ; that be enough . 

 its peculiar point of sweetness lie here . when the Mighty Heart 's yearning of love become too great for other expression , it become the sweet Rose of heaven , the beloved Man God . 
 Jesus ! you Jesus of our dream ! how we love you ; no Bible tell of you as we know you . your sweet hand hold our fast ; your sweet voice say always , " I be here , my loved one , not far off ; put your arm about I . " we find he in everything in those day . when the little weary lamb we drive home drag its foot , we seize on it , and carry it with its head against our face . his little lamb ! we feel we have get he . 
 when the drunken Kaffir lie by the road in the sun we draw his blanket over his head , and put green branch of milk - bush on it . his kaffir ; why should the sun hurt he ? 

 in the evening , when the cloud lift themselves like gate , and the red light shine through they , we cry ; for in such glory he will come , 

 and the hand that ache to touch he will hold he , and we shall see the beautiful hair and eye of our God . 

 " lift up your head , o ye gate ; and be ye lift up , ye everlaste door , and our king of glory shall come in ! " the purple flower , the little purple flower be his eye , look at we . we kiss they , and kneel alone on the flat , rejoice over they . 
 and the wilderness and the solitary place shall be glad for he , and the desert shall rejoice and blossom as a rose . if ever in our tearful , joyful ecstasy the poor , sleepy , half - dead devil should raise his head , we laugh at he . it be not his hour now . 
 " if there should be a hell , after all ! " he mutter . " if your God should be cruel ! if there should be no God ! if you should find out it be all imagination ! if " 

 we laugh at he . when a man sit in the warm sunshine , do you ask he for proof of it ? 

 he feel that be all . and we feel that be all . we want no proof of our God . we feel , we feel ! 

 do we believe in our God because the Bible tell we of he ? we believe in the Bible because he tell we of it . we feel he , we feel he , we feel that be all ! and the poor , half - swamp devil mutter 
 " but if the day should come when you do not feel ? " 
 and we laugh and cry he down . 
 " it will never come never , never , " and the poor Devil slink to sleep again , with his tail between his leg . fierce assertion many time repeat be hard to stand against . it be most wisely meet by silence . time separate the truth from the lie . so we dream on . 

 one day we go to town and to church . the townspeople rustle in in their silk , and the man in their sleek cloth , and settle themselves in their pew , and the light shin in through the window on the artificial flower in the 

 woman 's bonnet . we have the same miserable feeling that we have in a shop where all the clerk be very smart . we wish our Father have not   bring we to town , and we be out on the karroo . then the man in the pulpit begin to preach . his text be " he that believeth not shall be damn . " 

 the day before an atheist have die in the street , strike by lightning . 
 the man in the pulpit mention no name ; but he talk of " the hand of God make visible among we . " he tell we how , when the white stroke fall , quiver and naked , the soul flee , rob of his earthly filament , and lie at the footstool of God ; how over its head have be pour out the wrath of the Mighty One , whose existence it have deny ; and , quiver and terrify , it have flee to the everlasting night . 

 we , as we listen , half start up ; every drop of blood in our body have rush to our head . he lie ! he lie ! he lie ! that man in the 

 pulpit lie ! will no one stop he ? have none of they hear do none of they know , that when the poor , dark soul shut its eye on earth it open they in the still light of heaven ? that there be no wrath where God be ? that if one could once creep to the footstool of God , there be everlaste peace there ? while the atheist lie wonder and afraid , God bend down and say , " my child , 
 here 
 I be I , whom you have not know ; I , whom you have not believe in ; I be here . I send my messenger , the white sheet - lightning , to call you home . I be here . " 

 then the poor soul turn to the light its weakness and pain be go for ever . 
 have they not know , have they not hear , who it be rule ? 
 " for a little moment have I hide my face from thee ; but with everlasting kindness will I have mercy upon thee , saith the Lord thy Redeemer . " 

 we mutter on to ourselves , till some one pull 

 we violently by the arm to remind we we be in church . we see nothing but our own idea . 

 presently every one turn to pray . there be six hundred soul lift themselves to the Everlasting Light . 

 behind we sit two pretty lady ; one hand her scent - bottle softly to the other , and a mother pull down her little girl 's frock . one lady drop her handkerchief ; a gentleman pick it up ; she blush . the woman in the choir turn softly the leaf of their tune - book , to be ready when the praying be do . it be as though they think more of the singing than the Everlasting Father . oh , would it not be more worship of he to sit alone in the karoo and kiss one little field flower that he have make ? be it not mockery ? then the thought come , " 
 what doest thou here , Elijah ? 
 " we who judge , what be we well than they ? rather worse . be it any excuse to say we be but a child and must come ? do God allow any soul to step in 

 between the spirit he make and himself ? what do we there in that place , where all the word to we seem lie of the All Father , and the worship a seeming . fill with horror , we turn and flee out of the place . on the pavement we smite our foot , and swear in our child 's soul , never again to enter those place where man come to worship . we be question afterwards . why be it we go out of church ? 


 how can we explain ? we stand silent . then we be press far , and we try to tell . upon that a head be shake solemnly at we . 
 no one 
 can think it wrong to go to the house of the Lord ; it be the idle excuse of a wicked boy . when will we think seriously of our soul , and love go to church ? we be wicked , very wicked . and we we slink away and go alone to cry . will it be always so ? if we hate and doubt , or believe and love , to our dearest , be we to seem always wicked , wicked , wicked ? nothing else ! 


 we do not yet know that in the soul 's search for truth the bitterness lie here ; the strive can not always hide itself among the thought ; soon or later it will clothe itself in outward action ; then it step in and divide between we and our near . all thing on earth have their price ; and for truth we pay the dearest . we barter it for love and sympathy . the road to honour be pave with thorn ; but on the path to truth , at every step you set your foot down on your own heart . 


 VI . 
 then at last a new time the time of wake : short , sharp , and not pleasant . 
 Sleep and dream exist on this condition that no one wake the dreamer . 

 and life take we up between her finger and thumb , shake we furiously , till our poor 

 nodding head be well - nigh roll from our shoulder , and she set we down a little hard on the bare earth , bruised and sore , but preternaturally wide awake . 

 we have say in our day of dream , " injustice and wrong be a seem ; pain be a shadow . our God , he be real , he who make all thing , and he only be Love . " 

 now life take we by the neck and show we a few other thing , new - make graf with the red sand fly about they ; eye that we love with the worm eat they ; evil man walk sleek and fat , and she say , " what do you think of these ? " we dare not say " nothing . " we feel they ! we feel they ! they be very real . but we try to lay our hand about and feel that other thing we feel before . in the dark night in the fuel - room we cry to our beautiful dream - god : " oh , let we come near you , and lie our head against your foot . now in our hour of need be near 

 we . " but he be not there ; he be go away . the old questioning Devil be there ; but he be not there ; he be go away . 

 we must have be awaken soon or later . the imagination can not always triumph over reality , the desire over truth . we must have be awaken . if it be do a little sharply , what matter ? it be do thoroughly . 


 VII . 
 and a new life begin for we a new time : the old look indeed like a long hot delirium , people with phantasy . 

 now we have no God . we have have two : the old God that our father hand down to we , that we hat , and never like : the new one that we make for ourselves , that we love ; but one day he flit away with the feeling that give he birth , and we see what he be make 

 of the shadow of our high ideal , crown and throne . now we have no God ; we sit down without any . 

 " the fool hath say in his heart , " there be no god.í " it may be so . Most thing say or write have be the work of fool . 

 this 
 thing be certain 
 he 
 be a fool who say , " no man hath say in his heart , there be no God . " 

 it have be say many thousand time in heart with profound earnestess and bitter faith . 
 we do not cry and weep ; we sit down with great cold eye and look at the world . we be not miserable . why should we be ? we eat and drink , and sleep all night ; but the dead be not colder . 
 and we say it slowly , but without sigh , " yes , we see it now : there be no God . " 

 and , we add , grow a little cold yet , " there be no justice . the ox die in the yoke , beneath its master 's whip ; it turn its anguish- 

 fill eye on the sunlight , but there be no sign of recompense to be make it . the black man be shoot like a dog , and it go well with the shooter . the innocent be accuse and the accuser triumph . if you will take the trouble to scratch the surface anywhere , you will see under the skin a sentient be writhe in impotent anguish . " 

 and , we say far , and our heart be as the heart of the dead for coldness , " there be no orderer and no order : all thing be drive about by a blind chance . " 

 what a soul drink in with its mother 's milk will not leave it in a day . from our early hour we have be teach that the thought of the heart , the shaping of the rain - cloud , the amount of wool that grow on a sheep 's back , the length of a drought , and the grow of the corn , depend on nothing that move immutable , deep at the heart of all thing ; but on the changeable will of a changeable being , whom our prayer can 

 alter . to we , from the beginning , nature have be but a poor plastic thing , to be toy with this way or that , as man happen to please his deity or not ; to go to church or not ; to say his prayer right or not ; to travel on a Sunday or not . be it possible for we in an instant to see Nature as she be the flow vestment of an unchanging reality ? when the soul break free from the arm of a superstition , bit of the claw and talon break themselves off in he . it be not the work of a day to squeeze they out . 

 and so , for we , the human - like driver and guider be go , all existence , as we look out at it with our chill , wonder eye , be an aimless rise and swell of shift water . in all that welter chaos we can see no spot so large as a man 's hand on which we may plant our foot . 

 whether a man believe in a human - like God or no be a small thing . it be a great and terrible when he look into the mental and physical world and see no relation between cause 

 and effect , no order , but a blind chance sporting . it be almost a mercy to cut his throat , if indeed he do not do it for himself . 

 we , however , do not cut our throat . to do so would imply some desire and feeling , and we have no desire and no feeling ; we be only cold . we do not wish to live , and we do not wish to die . one day a snake curl itself round the waist of a Kaffir woman . we take it in our hand , swing it round and round , and fle it on the ground dead . every one look at we with eye of admiration . we almost laugh . be it bravery to risk that for which we care nothing ? 
 in truth , nothing matter . this dirty little world full of confusion , and the bit of blue stretch overhead for a sky , be worthless . 

 Existence , if it be not a dream , be a great pot , and the Fate who stir it round care nothing what rise to the top and what go down , and laugh when the bubble burst . and we do not care . let it boil about . why should we 

 trouble ourselves ? nevertheless the physical sensation be real . hunger hurt , and thirst ; therefore we eat and drink . inaction pain we ; therefore we work like galley - slave . no one demand it , but we set ourselves to build a great dam in red sand beyond the graf . in the grey dawn before the sheep be let out we be work at it . all day , while the young ostrich we tend feed about we , we work on through the fierce heat . the people wonder what new spirit have seize we now . they do not know we be work for our life . we bear the great stone , and feel a satisfaction when we stagger under they , and be hurt by a pang that shoot through our chest . while we eat our dinner we carry on basket full of earth , as though the devil drive we . the Kaffir servant have a story that at night a witch and two white oxen come to help we . no wall , they say , could grow so quickly under one man 's hand . 


 at night , alone in our cabin , we sit no more brooding over the fire . what should we think 

 of now ? it be all emptiness . so we take the old arithmetic ; and the multiplication table , which with so much pain we learn long ago and forget directly , we learn now in a few hour , and never forget again . we take a strange satisfaction in work arithmetical problem . we pause in our building to cover the stone with figure and calculation . we save money for a Latin Grammar and an Algebra , and carry they about in our pocket , pore over they as over our Bible of old . we have think we be utterly stupid , incapable of remember anything , of learn anything . now we find that all be easy . have a new soul creep into this old body , that even our intellectual faculty be change ? we marvel ; not perceive that what a man expend in prayer and ecstasy he can not have over for acquire knowledge . you never shed a tear , or create a beautiful image , or quiver with emotion , but you pay for it at the other end of your nature . you have just 

 so much force : when the one channel run over the other run dry . 

 and we turn to Nature . all these year we have live beside she , and we have never see she ; and now we open our eye and look at she . 
 the rock have be to we a blur of brown : we bend over they , and the disorganised mass dissolve into a many - colour , many - shape , carefully - arrange form of existence . here mass of rainbow - tint crystal , half- fuse together ; there band of smooth grey and red methodically overlying each other . this rock here be cover with a delicate silver tracery , in some mineral , resemble leaf and branch ; there on the flat stone , on which we so often have sit to weep and pray , we look down , and see it cover with the fossil footprint of great bird , and the beautiful skeleton of a fish . we have often try to picture in our mind what the fossile remain of creature must be like , and all the while we sit on they . 


 the flat plain have be to we a reach of monotonous red . we look at it , and every handful of sand start into life . that wonderful black people , the ant , we learn to know ; see they make war and peace , play and work , and build their huge palace . that small people we make acquaintance with also who live in the flower . the bitto flower have be for we a mere blur of yellow ; we find its heart compose of a hundred perfect flower , the home of the tiny black people with red stripe , who move in and out in that little yellow city . every bluebell have its inhabitant . every day the karroo show we a new wonder sleep in its teem breast . on our way back to work we pause and stand to see the ground spider make its trap , bury itself in the sand , and then wait for the fall in of its enemy . far on walk a horn beetle , and near he start open the door of a spider , who peep out carefully , and quickly pull it down again . on a karroo - bush a green fly be lay her silver egg . we 

 carry they home , and see the shell pierce , the spotted grub come out , turn to a green fly , and go away . we be not satisfied with what nature show we , and we see something for ourselves . under the white hen we put a dozen egg , and break one daily , to see the white spot wax into the chicken . we be not excited or enthusiastic about it ; but a man must think of something if he be to live at all . so we plant seed in row on our dam - wall , and pull one up daily to see how it go with they . Allardeen bury her wonderful stone , and a golden palace spring up at her foot . we do far more . we put a brown seed in the earth , and a live thing start out before our eye start upward why , no more than Allardeen can we say start upward , and do not desist till it be high than our head , sparkle with dew in the early morning , glitter with yellow blossom , shake brown seed with little embryo soul on to the ground . we look at it solemnly , from the time it be two small 

 leaf peep above the ground and a soft white root , till we have to raise our face to look at it ; but we find no reason for that upward start . 

 we look into dead duck and lamb . in the evening we carry they home , spread newspaper on the floor , and lie work with they till midnight . with a start feeling near akin to ecstasy we open the lump of flesh call a heart , and find little door and string inside . we feel they , and put the heart away ; but every now and then return to look , and to feel they again . why we like they so we can hardly tell . 

 a gander drown itself in our dam . we take it out , and open it on the bank , and kneel , look at it . above be the organ divide by delicate tissue ; below be the intestine , artistically curve in a spiral form , and each tier cover by a delicate network of blood - vessel , stand out red against the faint blue background . each branch of the blood - vessel be 

 comprise of a trunk , bifurcate and rebifurcate into the most delicate , hair - like thread , symmetrically arrange . we be strike with its singular beauty . and , moreover and here we drop from our kneeling into a sit posture this also we remark : of that same exact shape and outline be our thorn - tree see against the sky in midwinter : of that shape also be delicate metallic tracery between our rock ; in that exact path do our water flow when without a furrow we lead it from the dam ; so shaped be the antler of the horn beetle . how be these thing relate that such deep union should exist between they all ? be it chance ? can it be ? or , be they not all the fine branch of one trunk , whose sap flow through we all ? that would explain it . we nod over the gander 's inside . 


 this thing we call existence ; be it not a something which have its root far down below in the dark , and its branch stretch far out 

 into the immensity above , which we among the branch can not see ? not a chance jumble ; a live thing , a whole , a 
 one 
 . 

 we nod over the gander ; then start up suddenly , look into the blue sky , throw the dead gander and the refuse into the dam , and go to work again . 
 and so , it come to pass in time , that the earth cease for we to be a weltering chaos . we walk in the great hall of the universe , our soul look up and round reverentially . nothing be despicable all be meaning - full ; nothing be small all be part of a whole , whose beginning and end we know not . the life that throb in we be a pulsation from it . 
 and so , it come to pass at last , that whereas the sky be at first a small blue rag stretch out over we , and so low that our hand might touch it , press down on we , it raise itself into an immeasurable blue arch over our head , and we begin to live again . 




 CHAPTER II . 
 waldo 's stranger . 

 waldo 
 lie on his stomach on the red sand . the small ostrich he herd wander about he , peck at the food he have cut , or at pebble and dry stick . on his right lie the graf ; to his leave the dam ; in his hand be a large wooden post cover with carving , at which he work . Doss lie before he , bask in the winter sunshine , and now and again cast an expectant glance at the corner of the near ostrich camp . the scrubby thorn - tree under which they lie yield no shade , but none be need in that glorious June weather , when in the hot part of the afternoon the sun be but pleasantly warm ; and 

 the boy carve on , not look up , yet conscious of the brown serene earth about he and the intensely blue sky above . 

 presently , at the corner of the camp , Em appear , bear a cover saucer in one hand and in the other a jug , with a cup in the top . she be grow into a premature little old woman , ridiculously fat , and wear long dress . the jug and saucer she put down on the ground before the dog and his master and drop down beside they herself , pant and out of breath . 
 " oh , Waldo ! as I come up the camp I meet some one on horseback ; and I do believe it must be the new man . " 
 the new man be an Englishman to whom the boer - woman have hire half the farm . 
 " Hum ! " say Waldo . 

 " he be quite young , " say em , " and he have brown hair , and beard curl close to his face , and such dark blue eye . and , Waldo , 

 I be so ashamed ! I be just look back to see , you know , and he happen just to be look back too , and we look right into each other 's face ; and he get red , and I get so red . " 

 " yes , " say Waldo . 
 " I must go now . perhaps he have bring we letter from the post from Lyndall . and you know he will have to stay with we till his house be build . I must get his room ready . good - bye ! " 
 she trip off again , and Waldo carve on at his post . Doss lie with his nose close to the cover saucer , and smell that some one have make nice little fat cake that afternoon . both be so intent on their occupation , that not till a horse 's hoof beat beside they in the sand do they look up to see a rider draw in his steed . 

 he be certainly not the stranger whom Em have describe . a dark , somewhat french - look little man of eight - and - twenty , rather stout , 

 with heavy , cloudy eye and point moustache . his horse be a fiery creature , well caparison ; a highly - finish saddle - bag hang from the saddle ; the man 's hand be glove , and he present the appearance an appearance rare on that farm of a well - dress gentleman . 


 in an uncommonly melodious voice he inquire whether he might be allow to remain there for an hour . Waldo direct he to the farm - house , but the stranger decline . he would merely rest under the tree , and give his horse water . he remove the saddle , and Waldo lead the animal away to the dam . when he return , the stranger have settle himself under the tree , with his back against the saddle . the boy offer he of the cake . he decline , but take a draught from the jug ; and Waldo lie down not far off , and fall to work again . it matter nothing if cold eye see it . it be not his sheep - shearing machine . with material love , as with human , we go mad once , love out , and 

 have do . we never get up the true enthusiasm a second time . this be but a thing he have make , labour over , love and like nothing more . 


 the stranger force himself low down in the saddle and yawn . it be a drowsy afternoon , and he object to travel in these out - of - the - world part . he like well civilized life , where at every hour of the day a man may look for his glass of wine , and his easy - chair , and paper ; where at night he may lock himself into his room with his book and a bottle of brandy , and taste joy mental and physical . the world say of he the all - knowing , omnipotent world , whom no lock can bar , who have the cat - like propensity of see well in the dark the world say that well than the book he love the brandy , and well than book or brandy , that which it have be well have he love less . but for the world he care nothing ; he smile blandly in its tooth . all life be an aimless dream ; if wine 

 and philosophy and woman keep the dream from become a nightmare , so much the well . it be all they be fit for , all they can be use for . there be another side to his life and thought , but of that the world know nothing and say nothing , as the way of the wise world be . 

 the stranger look from beneath his sleepy eyelid at the brown earth that stretch away , beautiful in spite of itself in that June sunshine ; look at the graf , the gable of the farm - house showing over the stone wall of the camp , at the clownish fellow at his foot , and yawn . but he have drunk of the hind 's tea , and must say something . 
 " your father 's place , I presume ? " he inquire sleepily . 
 " no ; I be only a servant . " 
 " dutch people ? " 
 " yes . " 
 " and you like the life ? " 
 the boy hesitate . 

 " on day like these . " 
 " and why on these ? " 
 the boy wait . 
 " they be very beautiful . " 
 the stranger look at he . it seem that as the fellow 's dark eye look across the brown earth they kindle with an intense satisfaction ; then they look back at the carving . 

 what have that creature , so coarse - clothe and clownish , to do with the subtle joy of the weather ? himself , white - handed and delicate , 
 he 
 might hear the music with shimmering sunshine and solitude play on the finely - string chord of nature ; but that fellow ! be not the ear in that great body too gross for such delicate muttering ? 

 presently he say , 
 " may I see what you work at ? " 

 the fellow hand his wooden post . it be by no mean lovely . the man and bird be almost grotesque in their laboured resemblance 

 to nature , and bore sign of patient thought . the stranger turn the thing over on his knee .

 " I teach myself . " 
 " and these zigzag line represent " 
 " a mountain . " 
 the stranger look .

 the boy mutter confusedly , 
 " only thing . " 
 the questioner look down at he the huge , unwieldy figure , in size a man 's , in right of his child - like feature and curl hair a child 's ; and it hurt he it attract he and it hurt he . it be something between pity and sympathy .

 he point with his thumb to a grave .

 " my father . "

"

 CHAPTER III . 
 GREGORY ROSE find his AFFINITY . 

 the 
 new man , Gregory Rose , sit at the door of his dwelling , his arm fold , his leg cross , and a profound melancholy seem to rest over his soul . his house be a little square daub - and - wattle building , far out in the " karroo , " two mile from the homestead . it be cover outside with a sombre coating of brown mud , two little pane be let into the wall for window . behind it be the " sheep - kraal , " and to the right a large dam , now principally

 he take out ink and paper ; there be a family crest and motto on the latter , for the

Old Rose himself , an honest english farmer , know nothing of his noble descent ; but his wife and daughter know especially his daughter . there be Roses in England who keep a park and date from the Conquest . so the colonial " Rose Farm " become " Rose Manor " in remembrance of the ancestral domain , and the claim of the Roses to noble blood be establish in their own mind at least .

 broken heart but a woman be at the bottom of it . we be not to study law , nor science , nor art , so we study you . there be never a nerve or fibre in a man 's nature but we know it . we keep six of you dance in the palm of one little hand , " she say , balance her outstretched arm gracefully , as though tiny being disport themselves in its palm . " there we throw you away , and you sink to the devil , " she say , fold her arm composedly . " there be never a man who say one word for woman but he say two for man , and three for the whole human race . " 

 she watch the bird peck up the last yellow grain ; but Waldo look only at she . 
 when she speak again it be very measuredly . 

 " they bring weighty argument against we when we ask for the perfect freedom of woman , " she say ; " but , when you come up to the objection , they be like pumpkin - devil , with 

 candle inside , hollow , and can not   bite . they say that woman do not wish for the sphere and freedom we ask for they , and would not use it ! 


 " if the bird 
 do 
 like its cage , and 
 do 
 like its sugar and will not leave it , why keep the door so very carefully shut ? why not open it , only a little ? do they know , there be many a bird will not break its wing against the bar , but would fly if the door be open . 


 " then they say again , " if woman have the liberty you ask for , they will be find in position for which they have not talent!í if two man climb one ladder , do you ever see the weak anywhere but at the foot ? the sure sign of fitness be success . the weak never win but where there be handicapping . nature , leave to herself , will as beautifully apportion a man 's work to his capacity as long age ago she graduate the colour on the bird 's breast . if we be not fit you give we to no purpose the 

 right to labour ; the work will fall out of our hand into those that be abler . " 

 she talk more quickly and eagerly as she go on , as one talk of that over which they have brood long , and which lie near their heart . 
 Waldo watch she intently . 

 " they say woman have one great and noble work leave they , and they do it ill . that be true ; they do it execrably . it be the work that demand the broad culture , and they have not even the narrow . the lawyer may see no deep than his law book , and the chemist see no far than the window of his laboratory , and they may do their work well . but the woman who do woman 's work need a many - side , multiform culture ; the height and depth of human life must strike an answer chord in she ; she must have knowledge of man and thing in many state , a wide catholicity 

 of sympathy , the strength that spring from knowledge , and the magnanimity which spring from strength . 
 we

 we

 " the mighty and noblest of human work be give to we , and we do it ill . send an untutored navvie to work into an artist 's studio , and see what you will find there ! and yet , thank God , we have this work , " she add quickly : " it be the one window through which we see into the great world of earnest labour . the mean girl who 

 dance and dress become something high when her child look up into her face and ask her question . it be the only education we have and which they can not take from we . " 

 " and they say , " she go on , " that we complain of woman 's be compel to look upon marriage as a profession ; but that she be free to enter upon it or leave it , as she please . 

 " yes and a cat set afloat in a pond be free to sit in the tub till it die , it be under no obligation to wet its foot ; and a drown man may catch at a straw or not , just as he like it be a glorious liberty ! let any man think for five minute of what old maidenhood mean to a woman and then let he be silent . be it easy to bear through life a name that in itself signify defeat ? to dwell , as nine out of ten unmarried woman must , under the finger of another woman ? be it easy to look forward to an old age without honour , without the reward 

 of useful labour , without love ? I wonder how many man there be who would give up everything that be dear in life for the sake of maintain a high purity . " 


 she laugh , a little laugh that be clear without be pleasant . " and then , when they have no other argument against we , they say " go on ; but when you have make woman what you wish , and her child inherit her culture , you will defeat yourself . Man will gradually become extinct from excess of intellect , the passion which replenish the race will die.í Fools ! " she say , curl her pretty lip ; " a Hottentot sit at the road - side , and feed on a rotten bone he have find there , and take out his bottle of cape - smoke and swill at it , and grunt with satisfaction ; and the cultured child of the nineteenth century sit in his arm - chair , and sip choice wine with the lip of a connoisseur , and taste delicate dish with a 

 delicate palate , and with a satisfaction of which the Hottentot know nothing . heavy jaw and slop forehead all have go with increase intellect ; but the animal appetite be there still refine , discriminative , but immeasurably intensify . fool ! before man forgave or worship , while they be weak on their hind leg , do they not eat and drink and fight for wife ? when all the latter addition to humanity have vanish , will not the foundation on which they be build remain ?  CHAPTER V. 
 TANT ' SANNIE hold an upsitting , and GREGORY write a letter . 

 it 
 be just after sunset , and Lyndall have not yet return from her first driving - lesson , when the lean coloured woman stand at the corner of the house to enjoy the evening breeze , see come along the road a strange horseman . very narrowly she survey he , as slowly he approach . he be attire in the deep mourning , the black crape round his tall hat totally conceal the black felt , and nothing but a dazzle shirt - front relieve the funereal tone of his attire . he ride much forward in his saddle , with his chin rest on the uppermost 

 of his shirt - stud , and there be an air of meek subjection to the will of Heaven , and to what might be in store for he , that bespoke itself even in the way in which he gently urge his steed . he be evidently in no hurry to reach his destination , for the nearer he approach to it the slacker do his bridle hang . the coloured woman have duly inspect he , dash into the dwelling . 

 " here be another one ! " she cry " a widower ; I see it by his hat . " 
 " Good Lord ! " say Tant ' Sannie ; " it be the seventh I have   have this month ; but the man know where sheep and good look and money in the bank be to be find , " she add , wink knowingly . " how do he look ? " 
 " Nineteen , weak eye , white hair , little round nose , " say the maid . 

 " then it be he ! then it be he ! " say Tant ' Sannie triumphantly ; " little Piet Vander Walt , whose 

 wife die last month two farm , twelve thousand sheep . I have   not see he , but my sister - in - law tell I about he , and I dream about he last night . " 

 here Piet 's black hat appear in the doorway , and the boer - woman draw herself up in dignified silence , extend the tip of her finger , and motion solemnly to a chair . the young man seat himself , stick his foot as far under it as they would go , and say mildly 
 " I be Little Piet Vander Walt , and my father be Big Piet Vander Walt . " 
 Tant ' Sannie say solemnly , " yes . " 
 " Aunt , " say the young man , start up spasmodically ; " can I off - saddle ? " 
 " yes . " 
 he seize his hat , and disappear with a rush through the door . 

 " I tell you so ! I know it ! " say Tant ' Sannie . " the dear Lord do not   send dream for nothing . 

 do not   I tell you this morning that I dream of a great beast like a sheep , with red eye , and I kill it ? be not   the white wool his hair , and the red eye his weak eye , and my kill he mean marriage ? get supper ready quickly ; the sheep 's inside and roaster - cake . we shall sit up to - night . " 


 to young Piet Vander Walt that supper be a period of intense torture . there be something overawe in that assembly of english people , with their incomprehensible speech ; and moreover , it be his first courtship ; his first wife have court he , and ten month of severe domestic rule have not raise his spirit nor courage . he eat little , and when he raise a morsel to his lip glance guiltily round to see if he be not observe . he have put three ring on his little finger , with the intention of stick it out stiffly when he raise a coffee - cup ; now the little finger be curl miserably among its fellow . it 

 be small relief when the meal be over , and Tant ' Sannie and he repair to the front - room . once seat there , he set his knee close together , stand his black hat upon they , and wretchedly turn the brim up and down . but supper have cheer Tant ' Sannie , who find it impossible long to maintain that decorous silence , and whose heart yearn over the youth . 

 " I be relate to your aunt Selena who die , " say Tant ' Sannie . " my mother 's step - brother 's child be married to her father 's brother 's step - nephew 's niece . " 
 " yes , aunt , " say the young man , " I know we be relate . " 
 " it be her cousin , " say Tant ' Sannie , now fairly on the flow , " who have the cancer cut out of her breast by the other doctor , who be not the right doctor they send for , but who do it quite as well . " 
 " yes , aunt , " say the young man . 

 " I have   hear about it often , " say Tant ' Sannie . " and he be the son of the old doctor that they say die on Christmas day ; but I do not   know if that be true . People do tell such awful lie . why should he die on Christmas day more than any other day ? " 
 " yes , aunt , why ? " say the young man meekly . 
 " do you ever have the toothache ? " ask Tant ' Sannie . 
 " no , aunt . " 

 " well , they say that doctor , not the son of the old doctor that die on Christmas day , the other that do not   come when he be send for , he give such good stuff for the toothache , that if you open the bottle in the room where any one be bad they get well directly . you could see it be good stuff , " say Tant ' Sannie ; " it taste horrid . 
 that 
 be a real doctor ! he use to give a bottle so high , " say the boer - woman , raise 

 her hand a foot from the table , " you could drink at it for a month and it would not   get do , and the same medicine be good for all sort of sickness croup , measle , jaundice , dropsy . 
 now 
 you have to buy a new kind for each sickness . the doctor be not   so good as they use to be . " 

 " no , aunt , " say the young man , who be try to gain courage to stick out his leg and clink his spur together . he do so at last . 
 Tant ' Sannie have notice the spur before ; but she think it show a nice manly spirit , and her heart warm yet more to the youth . 
 " do you ever have convulsion when you be a baby ? " ask Tant ' Sannie . 
 " yes , " say the young man . 
 " strange ! " say Tant ' Sannie ; " I have convulsion too . wonderful that we should be so much alike ! " 
 " Aunt , " say the young man explosively , " can we sit - up to - night ? "

 in the dining room em work at her machine , and Gregory sit close beside she , his great blue eye turn to the window where Lyndall lean out talk to Waldo .

 nevertheless , when all the rest of the house have

 on the day precede Tant ' Sannie 's wedding , Gregory Rose sit in the blaze sun on the stone wall behind his daub - and - wattle house . it be warm , but he be intently watch a small buggy that be be recklessly drive over the bush in the direction of the farmhouse . Rose , E. Rose , L. Rose , L. Rose , L.L.L.L. Rose . when he have cover the sheet , he look at it discontentedly a little while , then suddenly begin to write a letter . 






 " Beloved Sister , 


 " 
 it 
 be a long while since I last write to you , but I have have no time . this be the first morning I have be at home since I do not   know when . em always expect I to go down to the farm - house in the morning ; but I do not   feel as though I could stand the ride to - day . 

 " I have much news for you . 

 " Tant ' Sannie , Em 's boer step - mother , be to be married to - morrow . she be go to town to - day , and the wedding feast be to be at her

 at all 
 , Jemima ,

 CHAPTER IX . 
 LYNDALL 's stranger . 

 a FIRE 
 be burn in the unused hearth of the cabin . the fuel blaze up , and light the black rafter , and warm the fade red lion on the quilt , and fill the little room with a glow of warmth and light make bright by contrast , for outside the night be chill and misty . 


 before the open fire - place sit a stranger , his keen blue eye study the fire from beneath delicately - pencil , droop eyelid . one white hand play thoughtfully with a heavy flaxen moustache ; yet once he start , and for an instant the languid lid raise themselves : there be a keen , intent look upon the face as he listen 

 for something . then he lean back in his chair , fill his glass from the silver flask in his bag , and resume his old posture .

 " I say , " come if you wish.í " 

 " and I do wish . you give I a cold reception . "

 " a young farmer . " 
 " live here ? "

 " a fool . "

 you ask I what you might and what you might not do ? "

 " sometimes I wear it ; then I take it off and wish to throw it into the fire ; the next day I put it on again , and sometimes I kiss it . "

 " because , if I have be married to you for a year I should have come to my sens and see that your hand and your voice be like the hand and the voice of any other man . "

 of my heart , but not the right ; and this be the case , my affection for you be not of a duly elevated , intellectual and spiritual nature.í I like you when you get philosophical . "

I love you . I do not pretend that it be in any high , superhuman sense ; I do not say that I should like you as well if you be ugly and deform , or that I should continue to prize you whatever your treatment of I might be , or to love you though you be a spirit without any body at all . that be sentimentality for beardless boy . 

 every one not a mere child   and you be not a child , except in year   know what love between a man and a woman mean . I love you with that love .  he seem lose in consideration ; then he say , 

 " it be well to have you on those condition than not at all . if you 
 will 
 have it , let it be so . " 


 he sit look at she . on her face be the weary look that rest there so often now when she sit alone . two month have not pass since they part ; but the time have set its mark on she . he look at she carefully , from the brown , smooth head to the little crossed foot on the floor . a worn look have grow over the little face , and it make its charm for he strong . for pain and time , which trace deep line and write a story on a human face , have a strangely different effect on one face and another . 

 the face that be only fair , even very fair , they mar and flaw ; but to the face whose beauty be the harmony between that which speak from within and the form through which it speak , power be add by all that cause the outer man to bear more deeply the impress of the inner . the pretty woman fade with the rose on her cheek , and the girlhood that last an hour ; the beautiful woman find her fulness of bloom only when a past have write itself on she , and her power be then most irresistible when it seem go . 

 from under their half - close lid the keen eye look down at she . her shoulder be bent ; for a moment the little figure have forget its queenly bearing , and droop wearily ; the wide , dark eye watch the fire very softly . 
 it certainly be not in her power to resist he , nor any strength in she that make his own at that moment grow soft as he look at she . 

 he touch one little hand that rest on her knee . 
 " poor little thing ! " he say ; " you be only a child . " 
 she do not draw her hand away from his , and look up at he . 
 " you be very tired ? " 
 " yes . " 
 she look into his eye as a little child might whom a long day 's play have sadden . 
 he lift she gently up , and sit she on his knee . 
 " poor little thing ! " he say . 
 she turn her face to his shoulder , and bury it against his neck ; he wind his strong arm about she , and hold she close to he . when she have sit for a long while , he draw with his hand the face down , and hold it against his arm . he kiss it , and then put it back in its old resting - place . 

 " do not   you want to talk to I ? " 
 " no . " 
 " have you forget the night in the avenue ? " 
 he could feel that she shake her head . 
 " do you want to be quiet now ? " 
 " yes . " 
 they sit quite still , except that only sometimes he raise her finger softly to his mouth . 
 Doss , who have be asleep in the corner , wake suddenly , plant himself before they , his wiry leg move nervously , his yellow eye fill with anxiety . he be not at all sure that she be not be retain in her present position against her will , and be not a little relieved when she sit up and hold out her hand for the shawl . 
 " I must go , " she say . 
 the stranger wrap the shawl very carefully about she . 

 " keep it close around your face , Lyndall ; it be very damp outside . shall I walk with you to the house ? " 
 " no . lie down and rest ; I will come and wake you at three o'clock . " 
 she lift her face that he might kiss it , and , when he have kiss it once , she still hold it that he might kiss it again . then he let she out . he have seat himself at the fire - place , when she re - open the door . 
 " have you forget anything ? " 
 " no . " 
 she give one long , linger look at the old room . when she be go , and the door shut , the stranger fill his glass , and sit at the table sip it thoughtfully . 

 the night outside be misty and damp ; the faint moonlight , try to force its way through the thick air , make darkly visible the outline of the building . the stone and wall be moist , 

 and now and then a drop , slowly collect , fall from the eave to the ground . Doss , not like the change from the cabin 's warmth , run quickly to the kitchen door - step ; but his mistress walk slowly past he , and take her way up the wind foot - path that run beside the stone wall of the camp . when she come to the end of the last camp , she thread her way among the stone and bush till she reach the German 's grave . why she have come there she hardly know ; she stand look down . suddenly she bent and put one hand on the face of a wet stone . 

 " I shall never come to you again , " she say . 
 then she kneel on the ground , and lean her face upon the stone . 

 " dear old man , good old man , I be so tired ! " she say   for we will come to the dead to tell secret we would never have tell to the living . " I be so tired . there be light , there 

 be warmth , " she wail ; " why be I alone , so hard , so cold ? I be so weary of myself ! it be eat my soul to its core , self , self , self ! I can not bear this life ! I can not breathe , I can not live ! will nothing free I from myself ? " she press her cheek against the wooden post . " I want to love ! I want something great and pure to lift I to itself ! dear old man , I can not bear it any more ! I be so cold , so hard , so hard ; will no one help I ? " 

 the water gather slowly on her shawl , and fall on to the wet stone ; but she lie there cry bitterly . for so the live soul will cry to the dead , and the creature to its God ; and of all this cry there come nothing . the lifting up of the hand bring no salvation ; redemption be from within , and neither from God nor man ; it be work out by the soul itself , with suffering and through time . 

 Doss , on the kitchen door - step , shiver , and 

 wonder where his mistress stay so long ; and once , sit sadly there in the damp , he have drop asleep , and dream that old Otto give he a piece of bread , and pat he on the head , and when he wake his tooth chatter , and he move to another stone to see if it be dry . at last he hear his mistress 's step , and they go into the house together . she light a candle , and walk to the boer - woman 's bed - room . on a nail under the lady in pink hang the key of the wardrobe . she take it down and open the great press . from a little drawer she take fifty pound   all she have in the world , relocke the door , and turn to hang up the key . the mark of tear be still on her face , but she smile . 

 " fifty pound for a lover ! a noble reward ! " she say , and open the wardrobe and return the note to the drawer . 

 once in her own room , she arrange the 

 few article she intend to take to - morrow , burn her old letter , and then go back to the front - room to look at the time . there be two hour yet before she must call he . she sit down at the dressing - table to wait , and lean her elbow on it , and bury her face in her hand . the glass reflect the little brown head with its even parting , and the tiny hand on which it rest . presently she look up . the large , dark eye from the glass look back at she . she look deep into they . 


 " we be all alone , you and I , " she whisper ; " no one help we , no one understand we ; but we will help ourselves . " the eye look back at she . there be a world of assurance in their still depth . so they have look at she ever since she could remember , when it be but a small child 's face above a blue pinafore they have look from . " we shall never be quite alone , 

 you and I , " she say ; " we shall always be together , as we be when we be little . " 

 the beautiful eye look into the depth of her soul . 
 " we be not afraid ; we will help ourselves ! " she say . she stretch out her hand and press it over they on the glass . " dear eye ! we will never be quite alone till they part we ; till then ! " 



 CHAPTER X. 
 GREGORY ROSE have an IDEA . 

 GREGORY ROSE 
 be in the loft put it neat . outside the rain pour ; a six month ' drought have break , and the thirsty plain be drench with water . what it could not swallow run off in mad rivulet to the great " sloot , " that now foam like an angry river across the flat . even the little furrow between the farmhouse and the kraal be now a stream , knee - deep , which almost bear away the kaffir - woman who cross it . it have rain for twenty - four hour , and still the rain pour on . the fowl have collect a melancholy crowd in and about the waggon - house , and the 

 solitary gander , who alone have survive the six month ' want of water , walk hither and thither , print his web foot - mark on the mud , to have they wash out the next instant by the pelt rain , which at eleven o'clock still beat on the wall and roof with unabated ardour . 


 Gregory , as he work in the loft , take no notice of it beyond stuff a sack into the broken pane to keep it out ; and , in spite of the pelt and patter , Em 's clear voice might be hear through the open trap - door from the dining room , where she sit at work , sing the " Blue Waterí 


 " and take I away , 
 and take I away , 
 and take I away , 
 to the Blue Water " 


 that quaint , childish song of the people , that have a world of sweetness , and sad , vague yearning when sing over and over dreamily by a woman 's voice as she sit alone at her work . 

 but Gregory hear neither that nor yet the loud laughter of the Kaffir maid , that every now and again break through from the kitchen , where they joke and work . of late Gregory have grow strangely impervious to the sound and sight about he . his lease have run out , but Em have say , " do not renew it ; I need one to help I ; just stay on . " and , she have add , " you must not remain in your own little house ; live with I ; you can look after my ostrich well so . " 


 and Gregory do not thank she . what difference do it make to he , pay rent or not , live there or not ; it be all one . but yet he come . Em wish that he would still sometimes talk of the strength of the master - right of man ; but Gregory be as one smite on the cheek - bone . she might do what she please , he would find no fault , have no word to say . he have forget that it be man 's right to rule . on that 

 rainy morning he have light his pipe at the kitchen fire , and when breakfast be over stand in the front door watch the water rush down the road till the pipe die out in his mouth . em see she must do something for he , and find he a large calico duster . he have sometimes talk of put the loft neat , and to - day she could find nothing else for he to do . so she have the ladder put to the trap - door that he need not go out in the wet , and Gregory with the broom and duster mount to the loft . once at work he work hard . he dust down the very rafter , and clean the broken candle mould and bent fork that have stick in the thatch for twenty year . he place the black bottle neatly in row on an old box in the corner , and pile the skin on one another , and sort the rubbish in all the box ; and at eleven o'clock his work be almost do . he seat himself on the packing - case which have 

 once hold Waldo 's book , and proceed to examine the content of another which he have not yet look at . it be carelessly nail down . he loosen one plank , and begin to lift out various article of female attire old - fashioned cap , apron , dress with long point body such as he remember to have see his mother wear when he be a little child . he shake they out carefully to see there be no moth , and then sit down to fold they up again one by one . they have belong to Em 's mother , and the box , as pack at her death , have stand untouched and forget these long year . she must have be a tall woman , that mother of Em 's , for when he stand up to shake out a dress the neck be on a level with his , and the skirt touch the ground . Gregory lay a night - cap out on his knee , and begin roll up the string ; but presently his finger move slow and slow , then his chin rest on his breast , and 

 finally the implore blue eye be fix on the frill abstractedly . when Em 's voice call to he from the foot of the ladder he start , and throw the nightcap behind he . 


 she be only come to tell he that his cup of soup be ready ; and , when he could hear that she be go , he pick up the night - cap again , and a great brown sun-"kapje " just such a " kapje " and such a dress as one of those he remember to have see a sister - of - mercy wear . Gregory 's mind be very full of thought . he take down a fragment of an old looking - glass from behind a beam , and put the " kapje " on . his beard look somewhat grotesque under it ; he put up his hand to hide it that be well . the blue eye look out with the mild gentleness that become eye look out from under a " kapje . " next he take the brown dress , and , look round furtively , slip it over his head . he have just get his arm in the sleeve , and be 

 try to hook up the back , when an increase in the patter of the rain at the window make he drag it off hastily . when he perceive there be no one come he tumble the thing back into the box , and , cover it carefully , go down the ladder . 

 Em be still at her work , try to adjust a new needle in the machine . Gregory drink his soup , and then sit before she , an awful and mysterious look in his eye . 
 " I be go to town to - morrow , " he say . 
 " I be almost afraid you will not   be able to go , " say Em , who be intent on her needle ; " I do not   think it be go to leave off to - day . " 
 " I be go , " say Gregory . 
 em look up . 
 " but the " slootsí be as full as river ; you can not go . we can wait for the post , " she say . 
 " I be not go for the post , " say Gregory , impressively . 

 em look for explanation ; none come . 
 " when will you be back ? " 
 " I be not come back . " 
 " be you go to your friend ? " 
 Gregory wait , then catch she by the wrist . 
 " look here , em , " he say between his tooth , " I can not   stand it any more . I be go to she . " 
 since that day , when he have come home and find Lyndall go , he have never talk of she ; but Em know who it be who need to be speak of by no name . 
 she say , when he have release her hand , 
 " but you do not know where she be ? " 
 " yes , I do . she be in Bloemfontein when I hear last . I will go there , and I will find out where she go then , and then , and then ! I will have she . " 

 em turn the wheel quickly , and the ill - adjusted needle spring into twenty fragment .

 there be an answer he might have make , but it be his secret , and he do not choose to share it . he say only , 
 " I be go . " 
 " will you be go long , Gregory ? " 
 " I do not know ; perhaps I shall never come back . do what you please with my thing . I can not stay here ! " 
 he rise from his seat . 

 " People say , forget , forget ! " he cry , pace the room . " they be mad ! they be fool ! do they say so to man who be die of thirst forget , forget ? why be it only to we they say 

 so ? it be a lie to say that time make it easy ; it be afterward , afterward that it eat in at your heart ! 

 " all these month , " he cry bitterly , " I have live here quietly , day after day , as if I care for what I eat , and what I drank , and what I do ! I care for nothing ! I can not bear it ! I will not ! forget ! forget ! " ejaculate Gregory . " you can forget all the world , but you can not forget yourself . when one thing be more to you than yourself , how be you to forget it ? 
 " I read , " he say " yes ; and then I come to a word she use , and it be all back with I again ! I go to count my sheep , and I see her face before I , and I stand and let the sheep run by . I look at you , and in your smile , a something at the corner of your lip , I see she . how can I forget she when , whenever I turn , she be there , and not there ? I can not , I will not , live where I do not see she .
