I should have know at first she never could suffer I . who be I , what be I , that she should look at I ? it be right that she leave I ; right that she should not look at I . if any one say it be not , it be a lie ! I be not go to speak to she , " he add " only to see she ; only to stand sometimes in a place where she have stand before . " 



 CHAPTER XI . 
 an UNFINISHED letter . 

 GREGORY ROSE 
 have be go seven month . em sit alone on a white sheepskin before the fire . 


 the August night - wind , weird and shrill , howl round the chimney and through the cranny , and in wall and door , and utter a long low cry as it force its way among the cleft of the stone on the " kopje . " it be a wild night . the prickly pear tree , stiff and upright as it hold its arm , feel the wind 's might , and knock its flat leaf heavily together , till great branch break off . the Kaffirs , as they sleep in their straw hut , 

 whisper one to another that before morning there would not be an armful of thatch leave on the roof ; and the beam of the waggon - house creak and groan as if it be heavy work to resist the importunity of the wind . 

 Em have not go to bed . who could sleep on a night like this ? so in the dining room she have light a fire , and sit on the ground before it , turn the roaster - cake that lie on the coal to bake . it would save work in the morning ; and she blow out the light because the wind through the window - chink make it flicker and run ; and she sit sing to herself as she watch the cake . they lie at one end of the wide hearth on a bed of coal , and at the other end a fire burn up steadily , cast its amber glow over Em 's light hair and black dress , with the ruffle of crape about the neck , and over the white curl of the sheepskin on which she sit . 

 louder and more fiercely yet howl the 

 storm ; but Em sing on , and hear nothing but the word of her song , and hear they only faintly , as something restful . it be an old , childish song she have often hear her mother sing long ago 


 " where the reed dance by the river , 
 where the willow 's song be say , 
 on the face of the morning water , 
 be reflect a white flower 's head . " 




 she fold her hand and sing the next verse dreamily 


 " where the reed shake by the river , 
 where the moonlight 's sheen be shed , 
 on the face of the sleep water , 
 two leaf of a white flower float dead . 
 dead , dead , dead ! " 




 she echo the refrain softly till it die away , and then repeat it . it be as if , unknown to herself , it harmonize with the picture and thought that sit with she there alone in the firelight . she turn the cake over , while the 

 wind hurl down a row of brick from the gable , and make the wall tremble . 

 presently she pause and listen ; there be a sound as of something knock at the back - doorway . but the wind have raise its level higher , and she go on with her work . at last the sound be repeat . then she rise , light the candle and the fire , and go to see . only to satisfy herself , she say , that nothing could be out on such a night . 
 she open the door a little way , and hold the light behind she to defend it from the wind . the figure of a tall man stand there , and before she could speak he have push his way in , and be force the door to close behind he . 
 " Waldo ! " she cry in astonishment . 
 he have be go more than a year and a half . 

 " you do not expect to see I , " he answer , as he turn toward she ; " I should have sleep in the out - house , and not trouble you to - night ; 

 but through the shutter I see glimmering of a light . " 

 " come in to the fire , " she say ; " it be a terrific night for any creature to be out . shall we not go and fetch your thing in first ? " she add . 
 " I have nothing but this , " he say , motion to the little bundle in his hand . 
 " your horse ? " 
 " be dead . " 
 he sit down on the bench before the fire . 
 " the cake be almost ready , " she say ; " I will get you something to eat . where have you be wander all this while ? " 
 " up and down , up and down , " he answer wearily ; " and now the whim have seize I to come back here . em , " he say , put his hand on her arm as she pass he , " have you hear from Lyndall lately ? " 
 " yes , " say Em , turn quickly from he . 

 " where be she ? I have one letter from she , but that be almost eighteen month ago now just when she leave . where be she ? " 
 " in the Transvaal . I will go and get you some supper ; we can talk afterward . " 
 " can you give I her exact address ? I want to write to she . " 
 but Em have go into the next room . 
 when food be on the table she kneel down before the fire , turn the cake , babble restlessly , eagerly , now of this , now of that . she be glad to see he Tant ' Sannie be come soon to show she her new baby he must stay on the farm now , and help she . and Waldo himself be well content to eat his meal in silence , ask no more question . 
 " Gregory be come back next week , " she say ; " he will have be go just a hundred and three day to - morrow . I have a letter from he yesterday . " 

 " where have he be ? " 
 but his companion stoop to lift a cake from the fire . 
 " how the wind blow ! one can hardly hear one 's own voice , " she say . " take this warm cake ; no one 's cake be like mine . why , you have eat nothing ! " 
 " I be a little weary , " he say ; " the wind be mad to - night . " 
 he fold his arm , and rest his head against the fire - place , whilst she remove the dish from the table . on the mantel - piece stand an ink - pot and some sheet of paper . presently he take they down and turn up the corner of the table - cloth . 
 " I will write a few line , " he say ; " till you be ready to sit down and talk . " 

 Em , as she shake out the table - cloth , watch he bend intently over his paper . he have change much . his face have grow 

 thin ; his cheek be almost hollow , though they be cover by a dark growth of beard . 


 she sit down on the skin beside he , and feel the little bundle on the bench ; it be painfully small and soft . perhaps it hold a shirt and a book , but nothing more . the old black hat have a piece of unhemmed muslin twisted round it , and on his elbow be a large patch so fix on with yellow thread that her woman 's heart ache . only his hair be not change , and hang in silky beautiful wave almost to his shoulder . to - morrow she would take the ragged edge off his collar , and put a new band round his hat . she do not interrupt he , but she wonder how it be that he sit to write so intently after his long weary walk . he be not tired now ; his pen hurry quickly and restlessly over the paper , and his eye be bright . presently Em raise her hand to her breast , where lie the letter yesterday have bring 

 she . soon she have forget he , as entirely as he have forget she ; each be in his own world with his own . he be write to Lyndall . he would tell she all he have see , all he have do , though it be nothing worth relate . he seem to have come back to she , and to be talk to she now he sit there in the old house . 

 " and then I get to the next town , and my horse be tired , so I could go no far , and look for work . a shop - keeper agree to hire I as salesman . he make I sign a promise to remain six month , and he give I a little empty room at the back of the store to sleep in . I have still three pound of my own , and when you just come from the country three pound seem a great deal . 

 " when I have be in the shop three day I want to go away again . a clerk in a shop have the low work to do of all the people . it be 

 much well to break stone ; you have the blue sky above you , and only the stone to bend to . I ask my master to let I go , and I offer to give he my two pound , and the bag of mealie I have buy with the other pound ; but he would not . 

 " I find out afterward he be only give I half as much as he give to the other that be why . I have fear when I look at the other clerk that I would at last become like they . all day they be bow and smirk to the woman who come in ; smile , when all they want be to get their money from they . they use to run and fetch the dress and ribbon to show they , and they seem to I like worm with oil on . there be one respectable thing in that store it be the Kaffir storeman . his work be to load and unload , and he never need to smile except when he like , and he never tell lie . 

 " the other clerk give I the name of Old Salvation ; but there be one person I like very much . he be clerk in another store . he often go past the door . he seem to I not like other his face be bright and fresh like a little child 's . when he come to the shop I feel I like he . one day I see a book in his pocket , and that , make I feel near he . I ask he if he be fond of reading , and he say , yes , when there be nothing else to do . the next day he come to I , and ask I if I do not feel lonely ; he never see I go out with the other fellow ; he would come and see I that evening , he say . 
 " I be glad , and buy some meat and flour , because the grey mare and I always eat mealie ; it be the cheap thing ; and if you boil it hard you can not   eat much of it . I make some cake , and I fold my great coat on the box to make it soft for he ; and at last he come . 

 " " you have   get a rummy place here , í he say . 
 " you see there be nothing in it but packing - case for furniture , and it be rather empty . while I be put the food on the box he look at my book ; he read their name out aloud . " Elementary Physiology , í " First principles.í 
 " " golly!í he say ; " I have   get a lot of dry stuff like that at home I get for Sunday School prize ; but I only keep they to light my pipe with now ; they come in handy for that.í then he ask I if I have ever read a book call the " black - eyed creole.í " that be the style for I , í he say ; " there where the fellow take the nigger - girl by the arm , and the other fellow cut it off ! that be what I like.í 
 " but what he say after that I do not   remember , only it make I feel as if I be have a bad dream , and I want to be far away . 

 " when he have finish eat he do not 

 stay long ; he have to go and see some girl home from a prayer - meeting ; and he ask how it be he never see I walk out with any on Sunday afternoon . he say he have lot of sweetheart , and he be go to see one the next Wednesday on a farm , and he ask I to lend my mare . I tell he she be very old . but he say it do not   matter ; he would come the next day to fetch she . 

 " after he be go my little room get back to its old look . I love it so ; I be so glad to get into it at night , and it seem to be reproach I for bring he there . the next day he take the grey mare . on Thursday he do not bring she back , and on Friday I find the saddle and bridle stand at my door . 
 " in the afternoon he look into the shop , and call out , 

 " " Hope you get your saddle , Farber . your bag - of - bone kick out six mile from here . I will send you a couple of shilling to - morrow , 

 though the old hide be not   worth it . good morning.í 

 " but I spring over the counter , and get he by his throat . my father be so gentle with she ; he never would ride her up - hill , and now this fellow have murder she ! I ask he where he have kill she , and I shake he till he slip out of my hand . he stand in the door grin . 

 " " it do not   take much to kill 
 that 
 bag - of - bone , whose master sleep in a packing - case , and wait till his company 's finish to eat on the plate . should not   wonder if you feed she on sugar - bag , í he say ; " and if you think I have   jump she , you would well go and look yourself . you will find she along the road by the " aas - vogel " that be eat her.í 


 " I catch he by his collar , and I lift he from the ground , and I throw he out into the street , half - way across it . I hear the book - keeper say to the clerk that there be always 

 the devil in those mum fellow ; but they never call I Salvation after that . 

 " I be write to you of very small thing , but there be nothing else to tell ; it have be all small and you will like it . whenever anything have happen I have always think I would tell it to you . the back thought in my mind be always you . after that only one old man come to visit I . I have see he in the street often ; he always wear very dirty black clothe , and a hat with crape round it , and he have one eye , so I notice he . one day he come to my room with a subscription - list for a minister 's salary . when I say I have nothing to give he look at I with his one eye . 

 " " young man , í he say , " how be it I never see you in the house of the lord?í I think he be try to do good , so I feel sorry for he , and I tell he I never go to chapel . " young man , í he say , " it grieve I to hear such 

 godless word from the lip of one so young so far go in the path of destruction . young man , if you forget God , God will forget you . there be a seat on the right hand side as you go at the bottom door that you may get . if you be give over to the enjoyment and frivolity of this world , what will become of your never - die soul?í 

 " he would not go till I give he half - a - crown for the minister 's salary . afterward I hear he be the man who collect the pew - rent , and get a per centage . I do not   get to know any one else . 
 " when my time in that shop be do I hire myself to drive one of a transport - rider 's waggon . 

 " that first morning , when I sit in the front and call to my oxen , and see nothing about I but the hill with the blue come down to they , and the karroo bush , I be drunk ; I laugh ; my heart be throb till it hurt 

 I . I shut my eye tight , that when I open they I might see there be no shelf about I . there must be a beauty in buy and selling , if there be beauty in everything : but it be very ugly to I . my life as transport - rider would have be the good life in the world if I have have only one waggon to drive . my master tell I he would drive one , I the other , and he would hire another person to drive the third . but the first day I drive two to help he , and after that he let I drive all three . whenever we come to an hotel he stop behind to get a drink , and when he ride up to the waggon he could never stand ; the Hottentot and I use to lift he up . we always travel all night , and use to " out - spaní for five or six hour in the heat of the day to rest . I plan that I would lie under a waggon and read for an hour or two every day before I go to sleep , and I do for the first 

 two or three ; but after that I only want to sleep , like the rest , and I pack my book away . when you have three waggon to look after all night , you be sometimes so tired you can hardly stand . at first when I walk along drive my waggon in the night it be glorious ; the star have never look so beautiful to I ; and on the dark night when we ride through the bush there be will - o'-the - wisps dancing on each side of the road . I find out that even the damp and dark be beautiful . but I soon change , and see nothing but the road and my oxen . I only wish for a smooth piece of road , so that I might sit at the front and doze . at the place where we " out - spannedí there be sometimes rare plant and flower , the festoon hang from the bush - tree , nut and insect , such as we never see here ; but after a little while I never look at they I be too tired . I eat as much as I could , and then lie down on my 

 face under the waggon till the boy come to wake I to " in - span , í and then we drive on again all night ; so it go , so it go . I think sometimes when I walk by my oxen I call to they in my sleep , for I know I think of nothing ; I be like an animal . my body be strong and well to work , but my brain be dead . if you have not feel it , Lyndall , you can not understand it . you may work , and work , and work , till you be only a body , not a soul . now , when I see one of those evil - look man that come from Europe navvy , with the beast - like , sunken face , different from any Kaffir 's I know what bring that look into their eye ; and if I have only one inch of tobacco I give they half . it be work , grind , mechanical work , that they or their ancestor have do , that have make they into beast . you may work a man 's body so that his soul die . work be good . I have work at the old farm from the 

 sun 's rise till its setting , but I have have time to think , and time to feel . you may work a man so that all but the animal in he be go ; and that grow strong with physical labour . you may work a man till he be a brute . I know it , because I have feel it . you will never understand the change that come over I . no one but I will ever know how great it be . but I be never miserable ; when I could keep my oxen from stick fast , and when I could find a place to lie down in , I have all I want . after I have drive eight month a rainy season come . for eighteen hour out of the twenty - four we work in the wet . the mud go up to the axle sometimes , and we have to dig the wheel out , and we never go far in a day . my master swear at I more than ever , but when he have do he always offer I his brandy - flask . when I first come he have offer it I , and I have always refuse ; but now I 

 drink as my oxen do when I give they water without think . at last I buy brandy for myself whenever we pass an hotel . 


 " one Sunday we " out - spannedí on the bank of a swollen river to wait for its go down . it be drizzle still , so I lie under the waggon on the mud . there be no dry place anywhere ; and all the dung be wet , so there be no fire to cook food . my little flask be fill with brandy , and I drink some and go to sleep . when I wake it be drizzle still , so I drink some more . I be stiff and cold ; and my master , who lie by I , offer I his flask , because mine be empty . I drink some , and then I think I would go and see if the river be go down . I remember that I walk to the road , and it seem to be go away from I . when I wake up I be lie by a little bush on the bank of the river . it be afternoon ; all the cloud have go , and the 

 sky be deep blue . the Bushman - boy be grill rib at the fire . he look at I and grin from ear to ear . " Master be a little nice , í he say , " and lie down in the road . something might ride over master , so I carry he there.í he grin at I again . it be as though he say , " you and I be comrade . I have lie in a road , too . I know all about it.í when I turn my head from he I see the earth , so pure after the rain , so green , so fresh , so blue ; and I be a drunken carrier , whom his leader have pick up in the mud , and lay at the roadside to sleep out his drunken booze . I remember my old life , and I remember you . I see how , one day , you would read in the paper " a german Carrier , name Waldo Farber , be kill through fall from his waggon , be instantly crush under the wheel . Deceased be suppose to have be drunk at the time of the accident.í there 

 be those notice in the paper every month . I sit up , and I take the brandy - flask out of my pocket , and I fling it as far as I could into the dark water . the Hottentot boy run down to see if he could catch it ; it have sink to the bottom . I never drink again . but , Lyndall , sin look much more terrible to those who look at it than to those who do it . a convict , or a man who drink , seem something so far off and horrible when we see he ; but to himself he seem quite near to we , and like we . we wonder what kind of a creature he be ; but he be just we , ourselves . we be only the wood , the knife that carve on we be the circumstance . 


 " I do not know why I keep on work so hard for that master . I think it be as the oxen come every day and stand by the yoke ; they do not know why . perhaps I would have be with he still ; but one day we start with 

 load for the Diamond Fields . the oxen be very thin now , and they have be stand about in the yoke all day without food , while the waggon be be load . not far from the town be a hill . when we come to the foot the first waggon stick fast . I try for a little while to urge the oxen , but I soon see the one " spaní could never pull it up . I go to the other waggon to loosen that " spaní to join they on in front , but the transport - rider , who be lie at the back of the waggon , jump out . 

 " " they shall bring it up the hill ; and if half of they die for it they shall do it alone , í he say . 

 " he be not drunk , but in bad temper , for he have be drunk the night before . he swear at I , and tell I to take the whip and help he . we try for a little time , then I tell he it be no use , they could never do it . he swear louder and call to the leader to come on with their whip , and 

 together they lash . there be one ox , a black ox , so thin that the ridge of his backbone almost cut through his flesh . 

 " " it be you , devil , be it , that will not pull?í the transport - rider say . " I will show you something.í he glower like a devil . 
 " he tell the boy to leave off flog , and he hold the ox by the horn , and take up a round stone and knock its nose with it till the blood come . when he have do they call to the oxen and take up their whip again , and the oxen strain with their back bent , but the waggon do not move an inch . 
 " " so you will not , will not   you?í he say . " I will help you.í 

 " he take out his clasp - knife , and run it into the leg of the trembling ox three time , up to the hilt . then he put the knife in his pocket , and they take their whip . the oxen 's flank quiver , and they foam at the mouth . 

 strain , they move the waggon a few foot forward , then stand with bent back to keep it from slide back . from the black ox 's nostril foam and blood be stream on to the ground . it turn its head in its anguish and look at I with its great start eye . it be pray for help in its agony and weakness , and they take their whip again . the creature bellow aloud . if there be a God , it be call to its Maker for help . then a stream of clear blood burst from both nostril ; it fall on to the ground , and the waggon slip back . the man walk up to it . 

 " " you be go to lie down , devil , be you ? we will see you do not   take it too easy.í 

 " the thing be just die . he open his clasp - knife and stoop down over it . I do not know what I do then . but afterward I know I have he on the stone , and I be kneel on he . the boy drag I off . I wish they 

 have not . I leave he stand in the sand in the road , shake himself , and I walk back to the town . I take nothing from that accursed waggon , so I have only two shilling . but it do not matter . the next day I get work at a wholesale store . my work be to pack and unpack good , and to carry box , and I have to work from six in the morning to six in the evening ; so I have plenty of time . I hire a little room , and subscribe to a library , so I have everything I need ; and in the week of Christmas holiday I go to see the sea . I walk all night to escape the heat , and a little after sunrise I get to the top of a high hill . before I be a long , low , blue , monotonous mountain . I walk look at it , but I be think of the sea I want to see . at last I wonder what that curious blue thing might be ; then it strike I , it be the sea ! I would have turn back again , only I be too tired . I 

 wonder if all the thing we long to see the church , the picture , the man in Europe will disappoint we so ! you see I have dream of it so long . when I be a little boy , mind sheep behind the " kopje;í I use to see the wave stretch out as far as the eye could reach in the sunlight . my sea ! be the idea always more beautiful than the real ? 

 " I get to the beach that afternoon , and I see the water run up and down on the sand , and I see the white foam breaker ; they be pretty , but I think I would go back the next day . it be not my sea . 

 " but I begin to like it when I sit by it that night in the moonlight ; and the next day I like it well ; and before I leave I love it . it be not like the sky and star , that talk of what have no beginning and no end ; but it be so human . of all the thing I have ever see , only the sea be like a human 

 be ; the sky be not , nor the earth . but the sea be always move , always something deep in itself be stir it . it never rest . it be always want , wanting , want . it hurry on ; and then it creep back slowly without have reach , moan . it be always ask a question , and it never get the answer . I can hear it in the day and in the night ; the white foam breaker be say that which I think . I walk alone with they when there be no one to see I , and I sing with they . I lie down on the sand and watch they with my eye half shut . the sky be well , but it be so high above our head . I love the sea . sometimes we must look down too . after five day I go back to the town . 


 " I have glorious book , and in the night I could sit in my little room and read they ; but I be lonely . book be not the same thing when you be live among people . I can not tell 

 why , but they be dead . on the farm they would have be live being to I ; but here , where there be so many people about I , I want some one to belong to I . I be lonely . I want something that be flesh and blood . once on this farm there come a stranger ; I do not ask his name , but he sit among the karroo and talk with I . now , wherever I have travel I have look for he in hotel , in street , in passenger waggon as they rush in , through the open window of house I have look for he , but I have not find he never hear a voice like his . one day I go to the Botanic Gardens . it be a half - holiday , and the band be to play . I stand in the long raise avenue and look down . there be many flower , and lady and child be walk about beautifully dress . at last the music begin . I have not hear such music before . at first it be slow and even , like the everyday life , when 

 we walk through it without thought or feeling ; then it grow fast , then it pause , hesitate , then it be quite still for an instant , and then it burst out . Lyndall , they make heaven right when they make it all music . it take you up and carry you away , away , till you have the thing you long for ; you be in their own world . the wall about you break , and you spread out , you be shut in on no side . I could not see anything while it be play ; I stand with my head against my tree ; but , when it be do , I see that there be lady sit close to I on a wooden bench , and the stranger who have talk to I that day in the karroo be sit between they . the lady be very pretty , and their dress beautiful . I do not think they have be listen to the music , for they be talk and laugh very softly . I hear all they say , and could even smell the rose on the breast of one . I be afraid he would 

 see I ; so I go to the other side of the tree , and soon they get up and begin to pace up and down in the avenue . all the time the music play they chat , and he carry on his arm the scarf of the prettiest lady . I do not hear the music ; I try to catch the sound of his voice each time he go by . when I be listen to the music I do not know I be badly dress ; now I feel so ashamed of myself . I never know before what a low , horrible thing I , dress in tancord , be . that day on the farm , when we sit on the ground under the thorn - tree , I think he quite belong to I ; now , I see he be not mine . 


 " at last they turn to go to the gate , and I walk after they . when they get out he help the lady into a phaeton , and stand for a moment with his foot on the step talk to they . he have a little cane in his hand , and an italian greyhound run after he . just when 

 they drive away one of the lady drop her whip . 

 " " pick it up , fellow , í she say ; and when I bring it she she throw sixpence on the ground . I might have go back to the garden then ; but I do not want music ; I want clothe , and to be fashionable and fine . I feel that my hand be coarse , and that I be vulgar . I never try to see he again . 

 " I stay in my situation four month after that , but I be not happy . I have no rest . the people about I press on I , and make I dissatisfied . I could not forget they . even when I do not see they they press on I , and make I miserable . I do not love book ; I want people . when I walk home under the shady tree in the street I could not be happy , for when I pass the house I hear music , and see face between the curtain . I do not want any of they , but I want 

 some one for mine , for I . I could not help it . 

 " only one day something make I happy . a nurse come to the store with a little girl belong to one of our clerk . while the maid go into the office to give a message to its father , the little child stand look at I . presently she come close to I and peep up into my face . 
 " " nice curl , pretty curl , í she say ; " I like curls.í 
 " she feel my hair all over , with her little hand . when I put out my arm she let I take she and sit she on my knee . she kiss I with her soft mouth . we be happy till the nurse - girl come and shake the little one , and ask she if she be not ashamed to sit on the knee of that strange man . but I do not think my little one minded . she laugh at I as she go out . 

 " if the world be all child I could like it ; but man and woman draw I so strangely , and then press I away , till I be in agony . I be not mean to live among people . perhaps some day , when I be grow old , I will be able to go and live among they and look at they as I look at the rock and bush , without let they disturb I , and take myself from I ; but not now . so I grow miserable ; a kind of fever seem to eat I ; I could not rest , or read , or think ; so I come here . I know you be not here , but it seem as though I should be near you ; and it be you I want you that the other people suggest to I , but can not give . " 

 he have fill all the sheet he have take , and now lift down the last from the mantelpiece . em have drop asleep , and lie slumber peacefully on the skin before the fire . out of door the storm still rag ; but in a fitful manner , as though grow half weary of itself . 

 he bend over his paper again , with eager flushed cheek , and write on . 


 " it have be a delightful journey , this journey home . I have walk on foot . the evening before last , when it be just sunset , I be a little footsore and thirsty , and go out of the road to look for water . I go down into a deep little " kloof.í some tree run along the bottom , and I think I should find water there . the sun have quite set when I get to the bottom of it . it be very still not a leaf be stir anywhere . in the bed of the mountain torrent I think I might find water . I come to the bank , and leap down into the dry bed . the floor on which I stand be of fine white sand , and the bank rise on every side like the wall of a room . above there be a precipice of rock , and a tiny stream of water ooze from they and fall slowly on to the flat stone below . each drop you 

 could hear fall like a little silver bell . there be one among the tree on the bank that stand cut out against the white sky . all the other tree be silent ; but this one shake and tremble against the sky . everything else be still ; but those leaf be quiver , quivering . I stand on the sand ; I could not go away . when it be quite dark , and the star have come , I creep out . do it seem strange to you that it should have make I so happy ? it be because I can not tell you how near I feel to thing that we can not see but we always feel . to - night have be a wild , stormy night . I have be walk across the plain for hour in the dark . I have like the wind , because I have seem force my way through to you . I know you be not here , but I would hear of you . when I use to sit on the transport waggon half - sleep , I use to start awake because your hand be on I . in 

 my lodging , night after night I have blow the light out , and sit in the dark , that I might see your face start out more distinctly . sometimes it be the little girl 's face who use to come to I behind the " kopjeí when I mind the sheep , and sit by I in her blue pinafore ; sometimes it be old . I love both . I be very helpless ; I shall never do anything ; but you will work , and I will take your work for mine . sometimes such a sudden gladness seize I when I remember that somewhere in the world you be live and work . you be my very own ; nothing else be my own so . when I have finish I be go to look at your room door " 

 he write ; and the wind , which have spend its fury , moan round and round the house , most like a tired child weary with cry . 

 em wake up , and sit before the fire , rub her eye , and listen , as it sob about the 

 gable , and wander away over the long stone wall . 

 " how quiet it have grow now , " she say , and sigh herself , partly from weariness and partly from sympathy with the tired wind . he do not answer she ; he be lose in his letter . 
 she rise slowly after a time , and rest her hand on his shoulder . 
 " you have many letter to write , " she say . 
 " no , " he answer ; " it be only one to Lyndall . " 
 she turn away , and stand long before the fire look into it . if you have a deadly fruit to give it will not grow sweet by keep . 
 " Waldo , dear , " she say , put her hand on his , " leave off writing . " 
 he throw back the dark hair from his forehead and look at she . 

 " it be no use write any more , " she say . 
 " why not ? " he ask . 
 she put her hand over the paper he have write . 
 " Waldo , " she say , " Lyndall be dead . " 



 CHAPTER XII . 
 GREGORY 's WOMANHOOD . 

 SLOWLY 
 over the flat come a cart . on the back seat sit Gregory , his arm fold , his hat draw over his eye . a Kaffir boy sit on the front seat driving , and at his foot sit Doss , who , every now and again , lift his nose and eye above the level of the splash - board , to look at the surround country ; and then , with an exceedingly knowing wink of his left eye , turn to his companion , thereby intimate that he clearly perceive his whereabouts . no one notice the cart come . Waldo , who be at work at his carpenter 's table in the waggon - house , see nothing , till chance to 

 look down he perceive Doss stand before he , the leg tremble , the little nose wrinkle , and a series of short , suffocate bark give utterance to his joy at reunion . 


 Em , whose eye have ache with look out across the plain , be now at work in a back - room , and know nothing till , look up , she see Gregory , with his straw hat and blue eye , stand in the door - way . he greet she quietly , hang his hat up in its old place behind the door , and for any change in his manner or appearance he might have be go only the day before to fetch letter from the town . only his beard be go , and his face be grow thin . he take off his leather gaiter , say the afternoon be hot and the road dusty , and ask for some tea . they talk of wool , cattle , and sheep , and Em give he the pile of letter that have come for he during that seven month ' absence , but of the 

 thing that lie at their heart neither say anything . then he go out to look at the kraal , and at supper Em give he hot cake and coffee . they talk about the servant , and then eat their meal in quiet . when it be end Gregory go into the front - room , and lie in the dark on the sofa . 

 " do you not want a light ? " em ask , venture to look in . 
 " no , " he answer ; then presently call to she , " come and sit here ; I want to talk to you . " 
 she come and sit on a footstool near he . 
 " do you wish to hear anything ? " he ask . 
 she whisper , " yes , if it do not hurt you . " 
 " what difference do it make to I ? " he say . " if I talk or be silent , be there any change ? " 

 yet he lie quiet for a long time . the light through the open door show he to she , 

 where he lay , with his arm throw across his eye . at last he speak . perhaps it be a relief to he to speak . 

 to Bloemfontein in the Free State , to which through an agent he have trace they , Gregory have go . at the hotel where Lyndall and her stranger have stay he put up ; he be show the very room in which they have sleep . the coloured boy who have drive they to the next town tell he in which house they have board , and Gregory go on . in that town he find they have leave the cart , and buy a spider and four grey , and Gregory 's heart rejoice . now indeed it would be easy to trace their course . and he turn his step northward . 

 at the farm - house where he stop the " oom " and " tante " remember clearly the spider with its four grey horse . at one place the boer - wife tell how the Englishman have buy milk , and ask the way to the next 

 farm . at the next farm the Englishman have buy a bunch of flower , and give half - a - crown for they to the little girl . it be quite true ; the boer - mother make she get it out of the box and show it . at the next place they have sleep . here they tell he that the great bull - dog , who hat all stranger , have walk in in the evening and lay its head in the lady 's lap . so at every place he hear something , and trace they step by step . 


 at one desolate farm the Boer have a good deal to tell . the lady have say she like a waggon that stand before the door . without ask the price the Englishman have offer a hundred and fifty pound for the old thing , and buy oxen worth ten pound for sixteen . the Dutchman chuckle , for he have the " salt - reim 's " money in the box under his bed . Gregory laugh too , in silence ; he could not lose sight of they now , so slowly they would have to move with that 

 cumbrous ox - waggon . yet , when that evening come , and he reach a little wayside inn , no one could tell he anything of the traveller . 


 the master , a surly creature , half stupid with boer - brandy , sit on the bench before the door smoke . Gregory sit beside he , question , but he smoke on . he remember nothing of such stranger . how should he know who have be there month and month before ? he smoke on . Gregory , very weary , try to wake his memory , say that the lady he be seek for be very beautiful , have a little mouth , and tiny , very tiny , foot . the man only smoke on as sullenly as at first . what be little , very little mouth and foot to he . but his daughter lean out in the window above . she be dirty and lazy , and like to loll there when traveller come , to hear the man talk , but she have a soft heart . presently a hand come out of the window , and a pair of velvet slipper touch his shoulder , tiny slipper 

 with black flower . he pull they out of her hand . only one woman 's foot have wear they , he know that . 

 " leave here last summer by a lady , " say the girl ; " might be the one you be look for . never see any foot so small . " 
 Gregory rise and question she . 
 they might have come in a waggon and spider , she could not tell . but the gentleman be very handsome , tall , lovely figure , blue eye , wear glove always when he go out . an english officer , perhaps ; no Africander , certainly . 
 Gregory stop she . 

 the lady ? well , she be pretty , rather , the girl say ; very cold , dull hair , silent . they stay for , it might be , five day ; sleep in the wing over against the " stoep " ; quarrelled sometimes , she think the lady . she have see everything when she go in to wait . one day the gentleman touch her hair ; she draw back 

 from he as though his finger poison she . go to the other end of the room if he come to sit near she . walk out alone . cold wife for such a handsome husband , the girl think ; she evidently pity he . they go away early one morning , how , or in which way , the girl could not tell . 

 Gregory inquire of the servant , but nothing more be to be learn ; so the next morning he saddle his horse and go on . at the farm he come to the good old " oom " and " tante " ask he to have coffee , and the little shoeless child peep out at the stranger from behind oven and gable ; but no one have see what he ask for . this way and that he ride to pick up the thread he have drop , but the spider and the waggon , the little lady and the handsome gentleman , no one have see . in the town he fare yet bad . 

 once indeed hope come to he . on the 

 " stoep " of an hotel at which he stay the night in a certain little village , there walk a gentleman , grave and kindly - looking . it be not hard to open conversation with he about the weather , and then ; have he ever see such and such people , a gentleman and a lady , a spider and waggon , arrive at that place . the kindly gentleman shake his head . what be the lady like , he inquire ? 

 Gregory paint . hair like silken floss , small mouth , underlip very full and pink , upper lip pink but very thin and curl ; there be four white spot on the nail of the forefinger , the eyebrow very straight . 
 " yes ; and a rose - bud tinge in the cheek ; hand like lily , and perfectly seraphic smile . " 
 " that be she ! that be she ! " cry Gregory . 

 who else could it be ? he ask where she 

 have go to . the gentleman most thoughtfully stroke his beard . he would try to remember . be not her ear . here such a violent fit of cough seize he that he run away into the house . an ill - fed clerk and a dirty barman stand in the door - way laugh aloud . Gregory wonder if they could be laugh at the gentleman 's cough , and then he hear some one laugh in the room into which the gentleman have go . he must follow he and try to learn more ; but he soon find that there be nothing more to be learn there . poor Gregory ! 


 Backward and forwards , backward and forwards , from the dirty little hotel where he have drop the thread , to this farm and to that , ride Gregory , till his heart be sick and tired . that from that spot the waggon might have go its own way and the spider another be an idea that do not occur to he . at last he see 

 it be no use linger in that neighbourhood , and press on . 

 one day , come to a little town , his horse knock up , and he resolve to rest they there . the little hotel of the town be a bright and sunny place , like the jovial face of the clean little woman who keep it , and who trot about talk always talk to the customer in the tap - room , and to the maid in the kitchen , and to the passer - by when she could hail they from the window ; talk , as good - natured woman with large mouth and small nose always do , in season and out . 

 there be a little front parlour in the hotel , keep for stranger who want to be alone . Gregory sit there to eat his breakfast , and the landlady dust the room and talk of the great find at the Diamond Fields , and the badness of maid - servant , and the shameful conduct of the dutch parson in that town to the English 

 in- 
 inhabitant 


 habitant . Gregory eat his breakfast and listen to nothing . he have ask his one question , and have have his answer ; now she might talk on . 

 presently a door in the corner open and a woman come out a mozambiquer , with a red handkerchief twisted round her head . she carry in her hand a tray , with a slice of toast crumble fine , and a half - fill cup of coffee , and an egg break open , but not eat . her ebony face grin complacently as she shut the door softly and say , " good morning . " 
 the landlady begin to talk to she . 
 " you be not go to leave she really , Ayah , be you ? " she say . " the maid say so ; but I be sure you would not   do such a thing . " 
 the Mozambiquer grin . 
 " Husband say I must go home . " 
 " but she have not   get any one else , and will not   have any one else . come , now , " say the landlady . 

 the Mozambiquer only show her white tooth good - naturedly for answer , and go out , and the landlady follow she . 
 Gregory , glad to be alone , watch the sunshine as it come over the fuchsia in the window , and run up and down on the panel door in the corner . the Mozambiquer have close it loosely behind she , and presently something touch it inside . it move a little , then it be still , then move again ; then through the gap a small nose appear , and a yellow ear overlap one eye ; then the whole head obtrude , place itself critically on one side , wrinkle its nose disapprovingly at Gregory , and withdraw . through the half - open door come a faint scent of toilet vinegar , and the room be dark and still . 
 presently the landlady come back . 

 " leave the door open , " she say , bustle to shut it ; " but a darkey will be a darkey , and never carry a head on its shoulder like 

 other folk . not ill , I hope sir , " she say , look at Gregory when she have shut the bed - room door . 

 " no , " say Gregory , " no . " 
 the landlady begin put the thing together . 
 " who , " ask Gregory , " be in that room ? " 

 Glad to have a little innocent piece of gossip to relate , and some one willing to hear it , the landlady make the most of a little story as she clear the table . six month before a lady have come alone to the hotel in a waggon , with only a coloured leader and driver . eight day after a little baby have be bear . if Gregory stand up and look out at the window he would see a blue gum - tree in the grave - yard ; close by it be a little grave . the baby be bury there . a tiny thing , only live two hour , and the mother herself almost go with it . after a while she be well ; but one day she get 

 up out of bed , dress herself without say a word to any one , and go out . it be a drizzly day ; a little time after some one see she sit on the wet ground under the blue gum - tree , with the rain dripping from her hat and shawl . they go to fetch she , but she would not come until she choose . when she do she have go to bed and have not rise again from it ; never would , the doctor say . 

 she be very patient , poor thing . when you go in to ask she how she be she say always " well , " or " nearly well ! " and lie still in the darken room , and never trouble any one . the Mozambiquer take care of she , and she would not allow any one else to touch she ; would not so much as allow any one else to see her foot uncover . she be strange in many way , but she pay well , poor thing ; and now the Mozambiquer be go , and she would have to take up with some one else . 

 the landlady prattle on pleasantly , and now carry away the tray with the breakfast - thing . when she be go Gregory lean his head on his hand , but he do not think long .

" now to - night it have come to this . the die eye on the pillow look into the die eye in the glass ; they know that their hour have come . she raise one hand and press the stiff finger against the glass . they be grow very stiff . she try to speak to it , but she would never speak again . only ,

 have she find what she seek for something to worship ? have she cease from be ? who shall tell we ? there be a veil of terrible mist over the face of the Hereafter . 



 CHAPTER XIII . 
 dreams . 

 " 
 tell 
 I what a soul desire , and I will tell you what it be . " so run the phrase . 

 " tell I what a man dream , and I will tell you what he love . " that also have its truth . 
 for , ever from the early childhood to the late age , day by day , and step by step , the busy wake life be follow and reflect by the life of dream wake dream , sleep dream . weird , misty , and distort as the invert image of a mirage , or a figure see through the mountain mist , they be still the reflection of a reality . 

 on the night when Gregory tell his story , 

 Waldo sit alone before the fire , his untasted supper before he . he be weary after his day 's work too weary to eat . he put the plate down on the floor for Doss , who lick it clean , and then go back to his corner . after a time the master throw himself across the foot of the bed without undressing , and fall asleep there . he sleep so long that the candle burn itself out , and the room be in darkness . but he dream a lovely dream as he lie there . 


 in his dream , to his right rise high mountain , their top crown with snow , their side clothe with bush and bath in the sunshine . at their foot be the sea , blue and breezy , bluer than any earthly sea , like the sea he have dream of in his boyhood . in the narrow forest that run between the mountain and the sea the air be rich that the scent of the honey - creeper that hang from dark green bush , and through the velvety grass little stream run purl down into the 

 sea . he sit on a high square rock among the bush , and Lyndall sit by he and sing to he . she be only a small child , with a blue pinafore , and a grave , grave , little face . he be look up at the mountain , then suddenly when he look round she be go . he slip down from his rock , and go to look for she , but he find only her little footmark ; he find they on the bright green grass , and in the moist sand , and there where the little stream run purl down into the sea . in and out , in and out , and among the bush where the honey - creeper hung , he go look for she . at last , far off , in the sunshine , he see her gathering shell upon the sand . she be not a child now , but a woman , and the sun shine on her soft brown hair , and in her white dress she put the shell she gather . she be stoop , but when she hear his step she stand up , hold her skirt close about she , and wait for his coming . one hand she put 

 in his , and together they walk on over the glitter sand and pink sea - shell : and they hear the leaf talk , and they hear the water babble on their way to the sea , and they hear the sea singing to itself , singing , singing . 

 at last they come to a place where be a long reach of pure white sand ; there she stand still , and drop on to the sand one by one the shell that she have gather . then she look up into his face with her beautiful eye . she say nothing ; but she lift one hand and lay it softly on his forehead ; the other she lay on his heart . 
 with a cry of suppress agony Waldo spring from the bed , fling open the upper half of the door , and lean out , breathe heavily . 
 great God ! it might be only a dream , but the pain be very real , as though a knife run through his heart , as though some treacherous murderer creep on he in the dark ! the strong man draw his breath like a frightened woman . 

 " only a dream , but the pain be very real , " he mutter , as he press his right hand upon his breast . then he fold his arm on the door , and stand look out into the starlight . 

 the dream be with he still ; the woman who be his friend be not separate from he by year only that very night he have see she . he look up into the night sky that all his life long have mingle itself with his existence . there be a thousand face that he love look down at he , a thousand star in their glory , in crown , and circle , and solitary grandeur . to the man they be not less dear than to the boy they have be not less mysterious ; yet he look up at they and shudder ; at last turn away from they with horror . such countless multitude stretch out far into space , and yet not in one of they all be she ! though he search through they all , to the farth , 

 faint point of light , nowhere should he ever say , " she be here ! " to - morrow 's sun would rise and gild the world 's mountain , and shine into its thousand valley ; it would set and the star creep out again . year after year , century after century , the old change of nature would go on , day and night , summer and winter , seed - time and harvest ; but in none of they all would she have part ! 


 he shut the door to keep out their hideous shining , and because the dark be intolerable light a

 candle 

 , and pace the little room , fast and fast yet . he see before he the long age of eternity that would roll on , on , on , and never bring she . she would exist no more . a dark mist fill the little room . 


 " oh , little hand ! oh , little voice ! oh , little form ! " he cry ; " oh , little soul that walk with mine ! oh , little soul , that look so fearlessly down into the depth , do you exist no more for 

 ever for all time ? " he cry more bitterly : " it be for this hour this that man blind reason , and crush out thought ! for this hour this , this they barter truth and knowledge , take any lie , any creed , so it do not whisper to they of the dead that they be dead ! ah , God ! God ! God ! for a here - after ! " 

 Pain make his soul weak ; it cry for the old faith . they be the tear that fall into the new - make grave that cement the power of the priest . for the cry of the soul that love and lose be this , only this : " bridge over Death ; blend the here with the here - after ; cause the mortal to robe himself in immortality ; let I not say of my Dead that it be dead ! I will believe all else , bear all else , endure all else ! " 
 mutter to himself , Waldo walk with bent head , the mist in his eye . 

 to the soul 's wild cry for its own there be many answer . he begin to think of they .

 " you shall see she again , " say the Christian , the true Bible Christian . yes ; you shall see she again . 
 " and I see the dead , great and small , stand before God . and the book be open , and the dead be judge from those thing which be write in the book . and whosoever be not find write in the book of life be cast into the lake of fire , which be the second death .

 shall 
 see she again . " 

 in his bitterness Waldo laugh low : 
 " ha , I have long cease to hearken to your hellish voice . " 

 but yet another speak . 
 " you shall see she again , " say the nineteenth century Christian , deep into whose soul modern unbelief and thought have creep , though he know it not . he it be who use his Bible as the pearl - fisher use their shell , sort out gem from refuse ; he set his pearl after his own fashion , and he set they well . " and whose then shall she be at the resurrection of the dead?í "

 Waldo pace on , moan in agony and longing . 
 he hear the Transcendentalist 's high answer . 

 " what have you to do with flesh , the gross and miserable garment in which spirit hide itself ? you shall see she again . but the hand , the foot , the forehead you love , you shall see no more . the love , the fear , the frailty that be bear with the flesh , with the flesh they shall die . let they die ! there be that in man that can not die a seed , a germ an embryo , a spiritual essence . high than she be on earth , as the tree be high than the seed , the man than the embryo , so shall you behold she ; change , glorify ! " 

 high word , ring well ; they be the offering of jewel to the hungry , of gold to the man who die for bread . Bread be corruptible , gold be incorruptible ; bread be light , gold be heavy ; bread be common , gold be rare ; but the hungry man will barter all your mine for one morsel of bread . around God 's throne there may be choir and company of angel , cherubim

 and , truly , do not the heart love its own with the

 " Change be death , " he cry , " change be death ! who dare to say the body never die , because it turn again to grass and flower ? and yet they dare to say the spirit never die , because in space some strange unearthly be may have spring up upon its ruin . leave I ! leave I ! " he cry in frantic bitterness . " give I back what I have lose , or give I nothing ! " 

 for the soul 's fierce cry for immortality be this this only : return to I after death the thing as it be before . leave I in the here - after the being that I be to - day . rob I of the thought , the feeling , the desire that be my life , and you have leave nothing to take . your immortality be annihilation , your here - after be a lie . 
 Waldo fling open the door , and walk out into the starlight , his pain - stricken thought ever drive he on as he pace there . 

 " there must be a here - after because man long for it ? " he whisper . " be not all life from the cradle to the grave one long yearn for that which we never touch ? there must be a here - after because we can not think of any end to life . can we think of a beginning ? be it easy to say " I be notí than to say " I shall not beí ? and yet , where be we ninety year ago ? dream , dream ! 

 ah , all dream and lie ! no ground anywhere . "

 for , mark you , man 
 will 
 dream ; the most that can be ask of they be but that the dream be not in too glaring discord with the thing they know . he walk with bent head .

" he mutter ; " the rose be red with the matter that once redden the cheek of the child ; the flower bloom the fairest on the last year 's battle - ground ; the work of death 's finger cunningly wreathe over be at the heart of all thing , even of the living . death 's finger be everywhere . the rock be build up of a life that be . body , thought , and love die : from where spring that whisper to the tiny soul of man , " you shall not dieí ? ah , be there no truth of which this dream be shadow ? "

 " no death , no death , " he mutter ; " there be that which never die which abide . it be but the individual that perishe , the whole remain . it be the organism that vanish , the atom be there . it be but the man that die , the Universal Whole of which he be part rework he into its inmost self . ah , what matter that man 's day be short ! that the sunrise see he , and the sunset see his grave ; that of which he be but the breath have breathe he forth and draw he back again . that abide we abide . " 

 for the little soul that cry aloud for 

 con- 
 continue 


 tinued personal existence for itself and its beloved , there be no help . for the soul which know itself no more as a unit , but as a part of the Universal Unity of which the Beloved also be a part ; which feel within itself the throb of the Universal Life ; for that soul there be no death . 

 " let we die , beloved , you and I , that we may pass on forever through the Universal Life ! " in that deep world of contemplation all fierce desire die out , and peace come down . he , Waldo , as he walk there , see no more the world that be about he ; cry out no more for the thing that he have lose . his soul rest . be it only John , think you , who see the heaven open ? the dreamer see it every day .

 so age succeed age , and dream succeed dream , and of the joy of the dreamer no man knoweth but he who dreameth . 
 our father have their dream ; we have our ; the generation that follow will have its own . without dream and phantom man can not exist .

 sit there with his arm fold on his knee , and his hat slouch down over his face , Waldo look out into the yellow sunshine that tint even the very air with the colour of ripe corn , and be happy . 

 he be an uncouth creature with small learning , and no prospect in the future but that of make endless table and stone - wall , yet it seem to he as he sit there that life be a rare and very rich thing . he rub his hand in the sunshine . ah , to live on so , year after year , how well ! always in the present ; let each day glide , bring its 

 own labour , and its own beauty ; the gradual lighting up of the hill , night and the star , fire - light and the coal ! to live on so , calmly , far from the path of man ; and to look at the life of cloud and insect ; to look deep into the heart of flower , and see how lovingly the pistil and the stamen nestle there together ; and to see in the thorn - pod how the little seed suck their life through the delicate curl - up string , and how the little embryo sleep inside ! well , how well , to sit so on one side take no part in the world 's life ; but when great man blossom into book look into those flower also , to see how the world of man too open beautifully , leaf after leaf . ah ! life be delicious ; well to live long , and see the darkness break , and the day come ! the day when soul shall not thrust back soul that would come to it ; when man shall not be drive to seek solitude because of the crying out of their 

 heart for love and sympathy . well to live long and see the new time break . well to live long ; life be sweet , sweet , sweet ! in his breast pocket , where of old the broken slate use to be , there be now a little dancing - shoe of his friend who be sleep . he could feel it when he fold his arm tight against his breast ; and that be well also . he draw his hat lower over his eye and sit so motionless that the chicken think he be asleep , and gather close around he . one even venture to peck at his boot ; but he run away quickly . tiny , yellow fellow that he be , he know that man be dangerous ; even sleep they might awake . but Waldo do not sleep , and come back from his sunshiny dream , stretch out his hand for the tiny thing to mount . but the chicken eye the hand askance , and then run off to hide under 

 its mother 's wing , and from beneath it it sometimes put out its round head to peep at the great figure sit there . presently its brother run off after a little white moth , and it run out to join they ; and when the moth flutter away over their head they stand look up disappointed , and then run back to their mother . 


 Waldo through his half - close eye look at they . think , fear , craving , those tiny spark of brother life , what be they , so real there in that old yard on that sunshiny afternoon ? a few year where would they be ? strange little brother spirit ! he stretch his hand toward they , for his heart go out to they ; but not one of the little creature come near he , and he watch they gravely for a time ; then he smile , and begin mutter to himself after his old fashion . afterward he fold his arm upon his knee , and rest his 

 forehead on they . and so he sit there in the yellow sunshine , muttering , muttering , muttering , to himself . 

 it be not very long after when Em come out at the back - door with a towel throw across her head , and in her hand a cup of milk . 
 " ah , " she say , come close to he , " he be sleep now . he will find it when he wake , and be glad of it . " 
 she put it down upon the ground beside he . the mother - hen be at work still among the stone , but the chicken have climb about he and be perch on he . one stand upon his shoulder , and rub its little head softly against his black curl : another try to balance itself on the very edge of the old feel hat . one tiny fellow stand upon his hand , and try to crow ; another have nestle itself down comfortably on the old coat - sleeve , and go to sleep there . 

 Em do not drive they away ; but she cover the glass softly at his side . " he will wake soon , " she say , " and be glad of it . " 
 but the chicken be wise . 

 the END .
